       <div id="content">
        <div id="content-1-topic">
         <article class="post">
          <div class="post-holder">
           <a class="less show-less-btn show_less_article_text" href="#">
            Show Less
           </a>
           <div class="topic-image img-holder " id="topic-image-holder">
            <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:GE_Building_Oct_2005.jpg" id="jTopicImage_1_src" target="_blank">
             <img class="topic-image-portrait-wide jTopicImage jTopicImageBig" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="21780" data-topic-title="NBC" id="jTopicImage_1" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/GE_Building_Oct_2005.jpg"/>
             <span class="copyright wait-to-display">
              
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div id="topic-article">
            <div id="main-topic-news">
            </div>
            <p>
             The
             <b>
              National Broadcasting Company
             </b>
             (
             <b>
              NBC
             </b>
             ) is an American commercial broadcast television and radio network that is the flagship property of NBCUniversal, a subsidiary of Comcast. The network is headquartered in the Comcast Building (formerly known as the GE Building) at Rockefeller Center in New York City, with additional major offices near Los Angeles (at Universal City Plaza) and in Chicago (at the NBC Tower). NBC is sometimes referred to as the "Peacock Network", in reference to its stylized peacock logo, which was originally created in 1956 for its then-new color broadcasts and became the network's official emblem in 1979.
            </p>
            <a class="more show_more_article_text_btn" href="#" id="show_more_article_text_short">
             Show More
            </a>
            <div class="show_less_article_text">
             <p>
              Founded in 1926 by the Radio Corporation of America (RCA), NBC is the oldest major broadcast network in the United States. In 1986, control of NBC passed to General Electric (GE)  which previously owned RCA and NBC until 1930, when it was forced to sell the companies as a result of antitrust charges  through its $6.4 billion purchase of RCA. Following the acquisition by GE (which later sold RCA), Bob Wright served as
             </p>
             <script type="text/javascript">
              Mediander.Ads.writeDiv('left_more');
             </script>
             <p>
              chief executive officer of NBC, remaining in that position until his retirement in 2007, when he was succeeded by Jeff Zucker. In 2003, French media company Vivendi merged its entertainment assets with GE, forming NBC Universal. Comcast purchased a controlling interest in the company in 2011, and acquired General Electric's remaining stake in 2013. Following the Comcast merger, Zucker left NBCUniversal and was replaced as CEO by Comcast executive Steve Burke.
              <br/>
              NBC has eleven owned-and-operated stations and nearly 200 affiliates throughout the United States and its territories, some of which are also available in Canada via pay television providers or in border areas over-the-air; NBC also maintains brand licensing agreements for international channels in South Korea and Germany.
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>
           <!-- /#topic-article -->
           <div class="showless">

             </span>
            </a>

                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-1">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-1" id="connection-excerpt-1">
                   <b>
                    CBS
                   </b>
                   (an initialism of the network's former name, the
                   <b>
                    Columbia Broadcasting System
                   </b>
                   ; corporate name
                   <b>
                    CBS Broadcasting, Inc.
                   </b>
                   ) is an American commercial broadcast television and radio network that is the flagship property of CBS Corporation. The company is headquartered at the CBS Building in New York City, with major production facilities and operations in New York City (at the CBS Broadcast Center) and Los Angeles (at CBS Television City, CBS Columbia Square and the CBS Studio Center).
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-1 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-1, .show-more-connection-article-1" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-1" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-1-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-1">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      CBS
                     </b>
                     (an initialism of the network's former name, the
                     <b>
                      Columbia Broadcasting System
                     </b>
                     ; corporate name
                     <b>
                      CBS Broadcasting, Inc.
                     </b>
                     ) is an American commercial broadcast television and radio network that is the flagship property of CBS Corporation. The company is headquartered at the CBS Building in New York City, with major production facilities and operations in New York City (at the CBS Broadcast Center) and Los Angeles (at CBS Television City, CBS Columbia Square and the CBS Studio Center).
                     <br/>
                     CBS is sometimes referred to as the
                     <b>
                      "Eye Network"
                     </b>
                     , in reference to the company's iconic logo, in use since 1951. It has also been called the
                     <b>
                      "Tiffany Network"
                     </b>
                     , alluding to the perceived high quality of CBS programming during the tenure of its founder William S. Paley. It can also refer to some of CBS's first demonstrations of color television, which were held in a former Tiffany &amp; Co. building in New York City in 1950.
                     <br/>
                     The network has its origins in United Independent Broadcasters Inc., a collection of 16 radio stations that was purchased by Paley in 1928, and renamed the Columbia Broadcasting System. Under Paley's guidance, CBS would first become one of the largest radio networks in the United States, and eventually one of the Big Three American broadcast television networks. In 1974, CBS dropped its full name and became known simply as CBS, Inc. The Westinghouse Electric Corporation acquired the network in 1995, renamed its corporate entity to the current name CBS Broadcasting, Inc. in 1997, and eventually adopted the name of the company it had acquired to become CBS Corporation. In 2000, CBS came under the control of Viacom, which was formed as a spin-off of CBS in 1971. In late 2005, Viacom split itself into two separate companies, and re-established CBS Corporation  through the spin-off of its broadcast television, radio and select cable television and non-broadcasting assets  with the CBS television network at its core. CBS Corporation is controlled by Sumner Redstone through National Amusements, which also controls the current Viacom.
                     <br/>
                     CBS continues to operate a radio network, which now mainly provides news and features content for its portfolio of owned-and-operated radio stations in large and mid-sized markets, and affiliated radio stations in various other markets. The television network has more than 240 owned-and-operated and affiliated television stations throughout the United States.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-1" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-1, #show-more-connection-article-1" href="#" id="show-less-1">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>

                </li>
               </ol>

                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ABC_77_W66_jeh.JPG" id="jTopicImage_3_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_3" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="62027" data-topic-title="American Broadcasting Company" id="jTopicImage_3" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/ABC_77_W66_jeh.JPG/128px-ABC_77_W66_jeh.JPG"/>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-2">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-2" id="connection-excerpt-2">
                   The
                   <b>
                    American Broadcasting Company
                   </b>
                   (
                   <b>
                    ABC
                   </b>
                   ) (stylized in its logo as
                   <b>
                    abc
                   </b>
                   since 1962; corporate name
                   <b>
                    American Broadcasting Companies, Inc.
                   </b>
                   ) is an American commercial broadcast television network that is owned by the DisneyABC Television Group, a subsidiary of Disney Media Networks division of The Walt Disney Company. The network is headquartered on Columbus Avenue and West 66th Street in Manhattan, with additional major offices and production facilities in New York City, Los Angeles and Burbank, California.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-2 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-2, .show-more-connection-article-2" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-2" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-2-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-2">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     The
                     <b>
                      American Broadcasting Company
                     </b>
                     (
                     <b>
                      ABC
                     </b>
                     ) (stylized in its logo as
                     <b>
                      abc
                     </b>
                     since 1962; corporate name
                     <b>
                      American Broadcasting Companies, Inc.
                     </b>
                     ) is an American commercial broadcast television network that is owned by the DisneyABC Television Group, a subsidiary of Disney Media Networks division of The Walt Disney Company. The network is headquartered on Columbus Avenue and West 66th Street in Manhattan, with additional major offices and production facilities in New York City, Los Angeles and Burbank, California.
                     <br/>
                     Since 2007, when ABC Radio (also known as Cumulus Media Networks) was sold to Citadel Broadcasting, ABC has reduced its broadcasting operations almost exclusively to television. The fifth-oldest major broadcasting network in the world, ABC is often nicknamed as "the Alphabet Network", as its acronym also represent the first three letters of the English alphabet.
                     <br/>
                     ABC originally launched on October 12, 1943 as a radio network, separated from and serving as the successor to the NBC Blue Network, which had been purchased by Edward J. Noble. It extended its operations to television in 1948, following in the footsteps of established broadcast networks CBS and NBC. In the mid-1950s, ABC merged with United Paramount Theatres, a chain of movie theaters that formerly operated as a subsidiary of Paramount Pictures. Leonard Goldenson, who had been the head of UPT, made the new television network profitable by helping develop and greenlight many successful series. In the 1980s, after purchasing an 80% interest in cable sports channel ESPN, the network's parent merged with Capital Cities Communications, owner of several print publications, and television and radio stations. In 1996, most of Capital Cities/ABC's assets were purchased by The Walt Disney Company.
                     <br/>
                     The television network has eight owned-and-operated and over 232 affiliated television stations throughout the United States and its territories. Most Canadians have access to at least one U.S.-based ABC affiliate, either over-the-air (in areas located within proximity to the CanadaUnited States border) or through a cable, satellite or IPTV provider; although most ABC programs are subject to simultaneous substitution regulations imposed by the Canadian Radio-television and Telecommunications Commission that allow pay television providers to replace an American station's signal with the feed of a Canadian broadcaster to protect domestic programming rights and advertising revenue. ABC News provides news and features content for select radio stations owned by Citadel Broadcasting, which purchased the ABC Radio properties in 2007.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-2" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-2, #show-more-connection-article-2" href="#" id="show-less-2">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>

                SHOW MORE
               </a>

                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-3" id="connection-excerpt-3">
                   <b>
                    The CW Television Network
                   </b>
                   (most commonly referred to as
                   <b>
                    The CW
                   </b>
                   ) is an American broadcast television network that is operated by The CW Network, LLC, a limited liability joint venture between CBS Corporation, the former owners of the United Paramount Network (UPN), and the Warner Bros. Entertainment subsidiary of Time Warner, former majority owner of
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-3 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-3, .show-more-connection-article-3" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-3" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-3-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-3">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      The CW Television Network
                     </b>
                     (most commonly referred to as
                     <b>
                      The CW
                     </b>
                     ) is an American broadcast television network that is operated by The CW Network, LLC, a limited liability joint venture between CBS Corporation, the former owners of the United Paramount Network (UPN), and the Warner Bros. Entertainment subsidiary of Time Warner, former majority owner of The WB Television Network. The "CW" name is derived from the first letters of the names of these corporations (
                     <u>
                      C
                     </u>
                     BS and
                     <u>
                      W
                     </u>
                     arner Bros.). The CW is sometimes referred to as the
                     <b>
                      "Green Network"
                     </b>
                     , in reference to the company's green logo.
                     <br/>
                     The network made its debut on September 18, 2006, after its two predecessors, UPN and The WB, respectively ceased independent operations on September 15 and September 17 of that year. The CW's first two nights of programming  on September 18 and 19, 2006  consisted of reruns and launch-related specials. The CW marked its formal launch date on September 20, 2006, with a two-hour season premiere of
                     <i>
                      America's Next Top Model
                     </i>
                     . The network's programming lineup is intended to appeal to people ranging in age from 18 to 34-years-old. The network currently runs programming six days a week: airing Monday through Fridays in the afternoon and in primetime, along with a Saturday morning live-action educational programming block produced by Litton Entertainment called
                     <i>
                      One Magnificent Morning
                     </i>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     The CW is also available in Canada on cable, satellite and IPTV providers through stations owned-and-operated by CBS Corporation and affiliates that are located within proximity to the CanadaUnited States border (whose broadcasts of CW shows are subject to simultaneous substitution laws imposed by the Canadian Radio-television and Telecommunications Commission, if a Canadian network holds the broadcast rights), and through three affiliates owned by Tribune Media that are classified in that country as superstations  New York City affiliate WPIX, Los Angeles affiliate KTLA and Chicago affiliate WGN-TV.
                     <br/>
                     The CW is also available in Mexico through affiliates located near the MexicoUnited States border (such as XETV-TDT/Tijuana-San Diego) on pay television providers. In both countries, some CW affiliates are receivable over-the-air in border areas depending on the station's signal coverage.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-3" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-3, #show-more-connection-article-3" href="#" id="show-less-3">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-4">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-4" id="connection-excerpt-4">
                   <b>
                    Nielsen ratings
                   </b>
                   are the audience measurement systems developed by Robert F. Elder and Louis F Woodruff and sold to Nielsen Company, in an effort to determine the audience size and composition of television programming in the United States. Nielsen Media Research was founded by Arthur C. Nielsen, a market analyst whose career had begun in
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-4 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-4, .show-more-connection-article-4" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-4" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-4-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-4">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Nielsen ratings
                     </b>
                     are the audience measurement systems developed by Robert F. Elder and Louis F Woodruff and sold to Nielsen Company, in an effort to determine the audience size and composition of television programming in the United States. Nielsen Media Research was founded by Arthur C. Nielsen, a market analyst whose career had begun in the 1920s with brand advertising analysis and had expanded into radio market analysis during the 1930s, culminating in Nielsen ratings of radio programming, which was meant to provide statistics as to the markets of radio shows. The first Nielsen ratings for radio programs were released the first week of December 1947. They measured the top 20 programs in four areas: total audience, average audience, cumulative audience and homes per dollar spent for time and talent.
                     <br/>
                     In 1950, Nielsen moved to television, developing a ratings system using the methods he and his company had developed for radio. That method has since become the primary source of audience measurement information in the television industry around the world.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-4" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-4, #show-more-connection-article-4" href="#" id="show-less-4">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-4 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-4" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-4" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-4-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

It was the first of its genre on American television and in the world, and is the fifth-longest-running American television series. Originally a two-hour program on weekdays, it expanded
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-5 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-5, .show-more-connection-article-5" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-5" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-5-short">

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-5">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <span>
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Today
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     (also called
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       The Today Show
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     ) is an American news and talk morning television show that airs on NBC. The program debuted on January 14, 1952. It was the first of its genre on American television and in the world, and is the fifth-longest-running American television series. Originally a two-hour program on weekdays, it expanded to Sundays (a one-hour program) in 1987 and Saturdays (running for two hours) in 1992. The weekday broadcast expanded to three hours in 2000, and to four hours in 2007.
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      Today
                     </i>
                     's dominance was virtually unchallenged by the other networks until the late 1980s, when it was overtaken by ABC's
                     <i>
                      Good Morning America
                     </i>
                     .
                     <i>
                      Today
                     </i>
                     retook the Nielsen ratings lead the week of December 11, 1995, and held onto that position for 852 consecutive weeks until the week of April 9, 2012, when it was beaten by
                     <i>
                      Good Morning America
                     </i>
                     yet again.
                     <i>
                      Today
                     </i>
                     has maintained its No. 2 status since the summer of 2012 each year behind
                     <i>
                      GMA
                     </i>
                     . In 2002,
                     <i>
                      Today
                     </i>
                     was ranked No. 17 on TV Guide's 50 Greatest TV Shows of All Time.
                    </p>

            <li class="connection" data-id="18581669" data-original-title="The DTV (an abbreviation of digital television, also called digital broadcast) transition in the United States is" data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="digital-television-transition-in" id="18581669" title="">
             <a data-topic-id="18581669" href="#!/18581669/digital-television-transition-in">
              <ol class="post-list">
               <li>
                <div class="connection-counter">
                 6
                </div>
                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="18581669" data-topic-title="Digital television transition in the United States" id="jTopicImage_7" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ab/Analog_Antenna.jpg/128px-Analog_Antenna.jpg"/>
                 <div class="connection-title-and-excerpt">
                  <span class="connection-title" data-count="6" data-id="18581669" data-url-title="digital-television-transition-in">
                   Digital television transition in the United States
                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   The DTV (an abbreviation of digital television, also called digital broadcast) transition in the United States is
                  </span>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </li>
              </ol>
             </a>
            </li>
            <!-- /Collapsed connection -->
            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="18581669" data-url-title="digital-television-transition-in" id="connection-expanded-6">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  6
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-6">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Analog_Antenna.jpg" id="jTopicImage_7_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_7" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="18581669" data-topic-title="Digital television transition in the United States" id="jTopicImage_7" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ab/Analog_Antenna.jpg/128px-Analog_Antenna.jpg"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-6">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-6" id="connection-excerpt-6">
                   The
                   <b>
                    DTV
                   </b>
                   (an abbreviation of
                   <b>
                    digital television
                   </b>
                   , also called
                   <b>
                    digital broadcast
                   </b>
                   )
                   <b>
                    transition in the United States
                   </b>
                   is the switchover from analog (the traditional method of transmitting television signals) to exclusively digital broadcasting of free over-the-air television programming. The transition from analog to digital television has been described by David Rehr, then president and CEO of
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-6 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-6, .show-more-connection-article-6" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-6" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-6-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-6">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     The
                     <b>
                      DTV
                     </b>
                     (an abbreviation of
                     <b>
                      digital television
                     </b>
                     , also called
                     <b>
                      digital broadcast
                     </b>
                     )
                     <b>
                      transition in the United States
                     </b>
                     is the switchover from analog (the traditional method of transmitting television signals) to exclusively digital broadcasting of free over-the-air television programming. The transition from analog to digital television has been described by David Rehr, then president and CEO of the National Association of Broadcasters, as representing "the most significant advancement of television technology since color TV was introduced." For full-power TV stations, the transition went into effect on Friday, June 12, 2009, with stations ending regular programming on their analog signals no later than 11:59pm local time that day.
                     <br/>
                     Under the Digital Transition and Public Safety Act of 2005, full-power broadcasting of analog television in the United States would have ceased after Tuesday February 17, 2009. To help U.S. consumers through the conversion, the Act also established a federally sponsored DTV Converter Box Coupon Program.
                     <br/>
                     The
                     <b>
                      DTV Delay Act
                     </b>
                     changed the mandatory analog cutoff date to June 12, although stations were permitted to cease analog transmissions before the new mandatory cutoff date. The legislation was enacted on February 4, 2009, and on February 11, 2009, President Barack Obama signed it into law. The purpose of the extension was to help the millions of households who had not been able to get their coupons for converters because demand for coupons exceeded the funding provided for in the initial bill, leaving millions on a waiting list to receive coupons. Funding for extra coupons was provided by the American Recovery and Reinvestment Act of 2009. By midnight on the original cut-off date of February 17, 2009, 641 stations representing 36 percent of U.S. full-power broadcasters were transmitting exclusively in digital.
                     <br/>
                     Analog broadcasting did not cease entirely following the June 12 deadline: under the provisions of the Short-term Analog Flash and Emergency Readiness Act, approximately 120 full-power stations briefly maintained analog "nightlight" service, ending no later than July 12. In a separate category, low power television stations will be permitted to continue analog broadcasts for several more years. In September 2010, the FCC announced a proposal to set a hard deadline of 2012 for low power stations to broadcast in digital.
                     <br/>
                     On July 15, 2011, the FCC posted the required transition deadlines for low power television. Stations broadcasting on channels 52 to 69 were required to vacate those channels by December 31, 2011, and all analog television transmitters (primarily low-powered (LP), and Class-A low-powered (-CA) stations, and also broadcast translator (TX) translator/repeaters in rural communities) must shut down by September 1, 2015. On April 24, 2015, it was announced that the conversion date for standard LPTVs and translators still broadcasting in analog has been suspended until further notice, due to economic problems that may arise from the upcoming spectrum auction; however, Class A low-powered stations are still required to convert by the original deadline date of September 1, 2015.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-6" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-6, #show-more-connection-article-6" href="#" id="show-less-6">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-6 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-6" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-6" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-6-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Digital television transition in the United States
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Some of these affiliates are also receivable over-the-air in southern areas of the country located near the CanadaUnited States border (signal coverage was somewhat reduced after the digital television transition in 2009 due to the lower radiated power required to transmit digital signals).
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Of 491 stations which had indicated their intention to go digital-only in February 2009, 123 affiliates of four major US commercial networks (ABC, CBS, Fox, NBC) were targeted by Federal Communications Commission opposition, precluding or applying additional restrictions to the shutdown of their analog signals in markets where the only analog service remaining after the February 17 shutdown would have been an independent or educational broadcaster, an adjacent-market station or a low-power station.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_television_transition_in_the_United_States" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Digital television transition in the United States
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  While 93 large-city network owned and operated stations (controlled by CBS, ABC, Fox TV and NBC) would continue analog broadcasts until June 12, many small-market broadcasters were unable to justify the extra cost, with non-commercial and independent stations very adversely affected.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_television_transition_in_the_United_States" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Digital television transition in the United States
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-6" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-6" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-6">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-6">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The FCC reserved final say on which stations would be allowed to transition on February 17 and which ones would be required to continue analog broadcasts, depending on how many viewers in each market have been determined not ready for the transition Owned &amp; Operated stations of five major networks (ABC, CBS, Fox, NBC and Telemundo, plus the CW, myNetworkTV and independent stations owned by CBS and myNetworkTV stations owned by Fox), as well as the station groups of Gannett, Hearst-Argyle and Meredith, committed to keeping all or most of their analog signals active until the new June 12 cutoff date.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_television_transition_in_the_United_States">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Digital television transition in the United States
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Similarly, Watertown, New York and Kingston, Ontario (which lack NBC locally) will lose Syracuse NBC affiliate WSTM-TV once the DTV transition renders Syracuse a UHF island.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_television_transition_in_the_United_States">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Digital television transition in the United States
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Syracuse, New York had since 1948 employed low-VHF channels to feed networks to adjacent markets (notably CBS to Utica, NBC to Watertown).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_television_transition_in_the_United_States">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Digital television transition in the United States
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   WECT (NBC 6 Wilmington), a signal which in its analog form reached to the edge of Myrtle Beach, could no longer be received by many who had watched the station for years a victim of a move to UHF 44 at a different transmitter site.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_television_transition_in_the_United_States">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Digital television transition in the United States
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   As the third network behind NBC and CBS, ABC had a hard time getting full-time affiliates even in larger markets, and Youngstown was fortunate enough to gain a full-time ABC affiliate in television's early years, as many markets comparable to Youngstown's size or even bigger didn't get one until the 1960s or even as late as the 1980s, while some very small markets didn't get one until the DTV transition in the 2000s.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WYTV">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WYTV
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                </ul>

                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bruce_Kennedy.jpg" id="jTopicImage_8_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_8" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="151921" data-topic-title="Emmy Award" id="jTopicImage_8" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bruce_Kennedy.jpg/128px-Bruce_Kennedy.jpg"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-7">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-7" id="connection-excerpt-7">
                   An
                   <b>
                    Emmy Award
                   </b>
                   , or simply
                   <b>
                    Emmy
                   </b>
                   , recognizes excellence in the television industry, and corresponds to the Academy Award (for film), the Tony Award (for theatre), and the Grammy Award (for music).
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-7 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-7, .show-more-connection-article-7" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-7" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-7-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-7">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     An
                     <b>
                      Emmy Award
                     </b>
                     , or simply
                     <b>
                      Emmy
                     </b>
                     , recognizes excellence in the television industry, and corresponds to the Academy Award (for film), the Tony Award (for theatre), and the Grammy Award (for music).
                     <br/>
                     Because Emmy Awards are given in various sectors of the American television industry, they are presented in different annual ceremonies held throughout the year. The two events that receive the most media coverage are the Primetime Emmys and the Daytime Emmys, which recognize outstanding work in American primetime and daytime entertainment programming, respectively. Other notable Emmy Award ceremonies are those honoring national sports programming, national news and documentary shows, national business and financial reporting, and technological and engineering achievements in television. Regional Emmy Awards are also presented throughout the country at various times through the year, recognizing excellence in local and statewide television. In addition, International Emmys are awarded for excellence in TV programming produced and initially aired outside the United States.
                     <br/>
                     Three related but separate organizations present the Emmy Awards: the Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences (ATAS), the National Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences (NATAS), and the International Academy of Television Arts &amp; Sciences (IATAS). Each is responsible for administering a particular set of Emmy ceremonies.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-7" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-7, #show-more-connection-article-7" href="#" id="show-less-7">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-7 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-7" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-7" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-7-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                   Ultra high frequency (UHF) is the ITU designation for radio frequencies in the range between 300 MHz and 3GHz

               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">

                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-8">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:UHF_TV_Antenna_001.JPG" id="jTopicImage_9_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_9" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="160501" data-topic-title="Ultra high frequency" id="jTopicImage_9" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/UHF_TV_Antenna_001.JPG/128px-UHF_TV_Antenna_001.JPG"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-8">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-8" id="connection-excerpt-8">
                   <b>
                    Ultra high frequency
                   </b>
                   (
                   <b>
                    UHF
                   </b>
                   ) is the ITU designation for radio frequencies in the range between 300 MHz and 3GHz, also known as the
                   <b>
                    decimetre band
                   </b>
                   as the wavelengths range from one to ten decimetres. Radio waves with frequencies above the UHF band fall into the SHF (super-high frequency) or microwave frequency range. Lower frequency
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-8 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-8, .show-more-connection-article-8" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-8" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-8-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-8">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Ultra high frequency
                     </b>
                     (
                     <b>
                      UHF
                     </b>
                     ) is the ITU designation for radio frequencies in the range between 300 MHz and 3GHz, also known as the
                     <b>
                      decimetre band
                     </b>
                     as the wavelengths range from one to ten decimetres. Radio waves with frequencies above the UHF band fall into the SHF (super-high frequency) or microwave frequency range. Lower frequency signals fall into the VHF (very high frequency) or lower bands. UHF radio waves propagate mainly by line of sight; they are blocked by hills and large buildings although the transmission through building walls is high enough for indoor reception. They are used for television broadcasting, cordless phones, walkie-talkies, personal radio services, satellite communication including GPS, cell phones and numerous other applications.
                     <br/>
                     The IEEE defines the UHF radar band as frequencies between 300MHz and 1GHz. Two other IEEE radar band overlap the ITU UHF band: the L band between 1 and 2GHz and the S band between 2 and 4GHz.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-8" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-8, #show-more-connection-article-8" href="#" id="show-less-8">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-8 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-8" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-8" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-8-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                   In the broadcasting industry (particularly in North America), a network affiliate or affiliated station is a local

                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-9">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_10_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_10" data-searched="" data-topic-id="17828038" data-topic-title="Network affiliate" id="jTopicImage_10" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-9">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-9" id="connection-excerpt-9">
                   In the broadcasting industry (particularly in North America), a
                   <b>
                    network affiliate
                   </b>
                   or
                   <b>
                    affiliated station
                   </b>
                   is a local broadcaster, owned by a company other than the owner of the network, which carries some or all of the programming lineup of a television or radio network. This distinguishes such a television or radio station from an owned-and-operated station (O&amp;O), which is owned by the parent network.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-9 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-9, .show-more-connection-article-9" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-9" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-9-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-9">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     In the broadcasting industry (particularly in North America), a
                     <b>
                      network affiliate
                     </b>
                     or
                     <b>
                      affiliated station
                     </b>
                     is a local broadcaster, owned by a company other than the owner of the network, which carries some or all of the programming lineup of a television or radio network. This distinguishes such a television or radio station from an owned-and-operated station (O&amp;O), which is owned by the parent network.
                     <br/>
                     Notwithstanding this distinction, it is common in informal speech (even for networks or O&amp;Os themselves) to refer to any station, O&amp;O or otherwise, that carries a particular network's programming as an affiliate, or to refer to the status of carrying such programming in a given market as an "affiliation".
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-9" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-9, #show-more-connection-article-9" href="#" id="show-less-9">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Network affiliate
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  The Orange Network name was removed from use in 1936, and the network's affiliate stations became part of the Red Network.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  On the other hand, several other television stations in the same market  WABC-TV (ABC), WCBS-TV (CBS), WNBC (NBC), WNJU (Telemundo), WNYW (Fox), WWOR-TV (MyNetworkTV), WPXN-TV (Ion Television), WXTV-DT (Univision) and WFUT-DT (UniMs)  are O&amp;Os.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Network_affiliate" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Network affiliate
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Generally, these markets had three VHF stations that were respectively affiliated with NBC, ABC and CBS (the then dominant television networks), one or more public television stations (which usually were member stations of PBS), and one or more UHF stations (and in the largest markets, such as New York City, Los Angeles and Chicago, at least one VHF station) without a network affiliation.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superstation" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>

                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>

            <li class="connection" data-id="763013" data-original-title="Saturday Night Live (abbreviated as SNL) is an American late-night live television sketch comedy and variety show" data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="saturday-night-live" id="763013" title="">
             <a data-topic-id="763013" href="#!/763013/saturday-night-live">
              <ol class="post-list">
               <li>
                <div class="connection-counter">
                 10
                </div>
                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="763013" data-topic-title="Saturday Night Live" id="jTopicImage_11" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/SNL_Original_Cast.jpg/128px-SNL_Original_Cast.jpg"/>

                  <span class="connection-title" data-count="10" data-id="763013" data-url-title="saturday-night-live">
                   Saturday Night Live
                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   Saturday Night Live (abbreviated as SNL) is an American late-night live television sketch comedy and variety show
                  </span>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </li>
              </ol>
             </a>
            </li>
            <!-- /Collapsed connection -->
            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="763013" data-url-title="saturday-night-live" id="connection-expanded-10">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  10
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-10">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:SNL_Original_Cast.jpg" id="jTopicImage_11_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_11" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="763013" data-topic-title="Saturday Night Live" id="jTopicImage_11" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/SNL_Original_Cast.jpg/128px-SNL_Original_Cast.jpg"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-10">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-10" id="connection-excerpt-10">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Saturday Night Live
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   (abbreviated as
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     SNL
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   ) is an American late-night live television sketch comedy and variety show created by Lorne Michaels and developed by Dick Ebersol. The show premiered on NBC on October 11, 1975, under the original title
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     NBC's Saturday Night
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   . The show's comedy sketches, which parody contemporary culture and politics, are performed by
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-10 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-10, .show-more-connection-article-10" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-10" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-10-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-10">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Saturday Night Live
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     (abbreviated as
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       SNL
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     ) is an American late-night live television sketch comedy and variety show created by Lorne Michaels and developed by Dick Ebersol. The show premiered on NBC on October 11, 1975, under the original title
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       NBC's Saturday Night
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     . The show's comedy sketches, which parody contemporary culture and politics, are performed by a large and varying cast of repertory and newer cast members. Each episode is hosted by a celebrity guest (who usually delivers an opening monologue and performs in sketches with the cast) and features performances by a musical guest. An episode normally begins with a cold open sketch that ends with someone breaking character and proclaiming, "Live from New York, it's Saturday Night!," beginning the show proper.
                     <br/>
                     In 1980, Michaels left the series to explore other opportunities. He was replaced by Jean Doumanian, who was replaced by Ebersol after a season of bad reviews. Ebersol ran the show until 1985, when Michaels returned; Michaels has remained since then. Many of
                     <i>
                      SNL
                     </i>
                     's cast found national stardom while appearing on the show, and achieved success in film and television, both in front of and behind the camera. Others associated with the show, such as writers, have gone on to successful careers creating, writing, or starring in TV and film.
                     <br/>
                     Broadcast from Studio 8H at NBC's headquarters in the Comcast Building,
                     <i>
                      SNL
                     </i>
                     has aired 787 episodes since its debut, and concluded its fortieth season on May 16, 2015, making it one of the longest-running network television programs in the United States. The show format has been developed and recreated in several countries, including Canada, Spain, Italy, South Korea, Japan, and Brazil each meeting with different levels of success. Successful sketches have seen life outside of the show as feature films, although only two met with critical and financial success:
                     <i>
                      The Blues Brothers
                     </i>
                     (1980) and
                     <i>
                      Wayne's World
                     </i>
                     (1992). The show has been marketed in other ways, including home media releases of "best of" and whole seasons, and books and documentaries about behind-the-scenes activities of running and developing the show.
                     <br/>
                     Throughout four decades on air,
                     <i>
                      Saturday Night Live
                     </i>
                     has received a number of awards, including 36 Primetime Emmy Awards, two Peabody Awards, and three Writers Guild of America Awards. In 2000, it was inducted into the National Association of Broadcasters Hall of Fame. It was ranked tenth in
                     <i>
                      TV Guide
                     </i>
                     's "50 Greatest TV Shows of All Time" list, and in 2007 it was listed as one of
                     <i>
                      Time
                     </i>
                     magazine's "100 Best TV Shows of All-
                     <i>
                      TIME
                     </i>
                     ". As of 2012, it has received 156 Emmy nominations, the most received by any TV show. The live aspect of the show has resulted in several controversies and acts of censorship, with mistakes and intentional acts of sabotage by performers as well as guests.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-10" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-10, #show-more-connection-article-10" href="#" id="show-less-10">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-10 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-10" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-10" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-10-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-11">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Seven_broadcast_centre.JPG" id="jTopicImage_12_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_12" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="2477490" data-topic-title="Owned-and-operated station" id="jTopicImage_12" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Seven_broadcast_centre.JPG/128px-Seven_broadcast_centre.JPG"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-11">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-11" id="connection-excerpt-11">
                   In the broadcasting industry, an
                   <b>
                    owned-and-operated station
                   </b>
                   (frequently abbreviated as
                   <b>
                    O&amp;O
                   </b>
                   ) usually refers to a television or radio station that is owned by the network with which it is associated. This distinguishes such a station from an affiliate, whose ownership lies elsewhere other than the network it is linked to.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-11 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-11, .show-more-connection-article-11" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-11" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-11-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-11">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     In the broadcasting industry, an
                     <b>
                      owned-and-operated station
                     </b>
                     (frequently abbreviated as
                     <b>
                      O&amp;O
                     </b>
                     ) usually refers to a television or radio station that is owned by the network with which it is associated. This distinguishes such a station from an affiliate, whose ownership lies elsewhere other than the network it is linked to.
                     <br/>
                     The concept of an O&amp;O is clearly defined in the United States and Canada (and to some extent, several other countries such as the United Kingdom, Australia, Brazil, and Japan), where network-owned stations had historically been the exception rather than the rule. In such places, broadcasting licenses are generally issued on a local (rather than national) basis, and there is (or was) some sort of regulatory mechanism in place to prevent any company (including a broadcasting network) from owning stations in every market in the country. In other parts of the world, many television networks were given national broadcasting licenses at launch; as such, they have traditionally been mostly (or entirely) composed of O&amp;Os, rendering a separate notion for such a concept redundant.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-11" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-11, #show-more-connection-article-11" href="#" id="show-less-11">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-11 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-11" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-11" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-11-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Owned-and-operated station
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  NBC has eleven owned-and-operated stations and nearly 200 affiliates throughout the United States and its territories, some of which are also available in Canada via pay television providers or in border areas over-the-air; NBC also maintains brand licensing agreements for international channels in South Korea and Germany.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  While 93 large-city network owned and operated stations (controlled by CBS, ABC, Fox TV and NBC) would continue analog broadcasts until June 12, many small-market broadcasters were unable to justify the extra cost, with non-commercial and independent stations very adversely affected.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_television_transition_in_the_United_States" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Digital television transition in the United States
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  <b>
                   WMAQ-TV
                  </b>
                  , channel 5, is an NBC owned-and-operated television station located in Chicago, Illinois, United States.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WMAQ-TV" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    WMAQ-TV
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-11" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-11" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-11">

                   </b>

                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KNBC">
                    from
                    <span>
                     KNBC
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   As an example of this centralized broadcast programming system on a large scale is NBC's "hub-spoke project" that enables "hub" cities such as New York City, Los Angeles, California, and Miami, Florida to originate television commercial, breaks and programming for many of its smaller individual stations, thus reducing or eliminating some responsibilities and employees of the local master control at NBC owned &amp; operated (O&amp;O) stations.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Master_control">

             <a data-topic-id="29697498" href="#!/29697498/pbs">
              <ol class="post-list">

                <div class="connection-counter">

                </div>
                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="29697498" data-topic-title="PBS" id="jTopicImage_13" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/KUHT_Big_Bird.jpg/128px-KUHT_Big_Bird.jpg"/>

            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="29697498" data-url-title="pbs" id="connection-expanded-12">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  12
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-12">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:KUHT_Big_Bird.jpg" id="jTopicImage_13_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_13" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="29697498" data-topic-title="PBS" id="jTopicImage_13" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/KUHT_Big_Bird.jpg/128px-KUHT_Big_Bird.jpg"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-12">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-12" id="connection-excerpt-12">
                   The
                   <b>
                    Public Broadcasting Service
                   </b>
                   (
                   <b>
                    PBS
                   </b>
                   ) is an American public broadcaster and television program distributor. Headquartered in Arlington, Virginia, PBS is an independently operated non-profit organization and is the most prominent provider of television programs to public television stations in the United States, distributing series such as
                   <i>
                    NOVA
                   </i>
                   ,
                   <i>
                    Sesame Street
                   </i>
                   ,
                   <i>
                    PBS NewsHour
                   </i>
                   ,
                   <i>
                    Masterpiece
                   </i>
                   ,
                   <i>
                    Nature, American Masters
                   </i>
                   ,
                   <i>
                    Frontline
                   </i>
                   , and
                   <i>
                    Antiques Roadshow
                   </i>
                   .
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-12 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-12, .show-more-connection-article-12" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-12" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-12-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-12">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     The
                     <b>
                      Public Broadcasting Service
                     </b>
                     (
                     <b>
                      PBS
                     </b>
                     ) is an American public broadcaster and television program distributor. Headquartered in Arlington, Virginia, PBS is an independently operated non-profit organization and is the most prominent provider of television programs to public television stations in the United States, distributing series such as
                     <i>
                      NOVA
                     </i>
                     ,
                     <i>
                      Sesame Street
                     </i>
                     ,
                     <i>
                      PBS NewsHour
                     </i>
                     ,
                     <i>
                      Masterpiece
                     </i>
                     ,
                     <i>
                      Nature, American Masters
                     </i>
                     ,
                     <i>
                      Frontline
                     </i>
                     , and
                     <i>
                      Antiques Roadshow
                     </i>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     Since the mid-2000s Roper polls commissioned by PBS have consistently placed the service as the most-trusted national institution in the United States. However, PBS is not responsible for all programming carried on public television stations, a large proportion of which (including most specials aired during multi-annually pledge drives) come from third-party sources, including member stations (such as WGBH, WETA-TV, WNET, WTTW National Productions), American Public Television and independent producers. This distinction is a frequent source of viewer confusion.
                     <br/>
                     The service has more than 350 member television stations, many owned by educational institutions or non-profit groups affiliated with a local public school district, collegiate educational institution or by state government-owned or -related entities. It also operates National Datacast (NDI), a subsidiary which offers datacasting services via member stations, and provides additional revenue for PBS and its member stations.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-12" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-12, #show-more-connection-article-12" href="#" id="show-less-12">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-12 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-12" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-12" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-12-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                PBS
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  On March 28, 2012, it was announced that NBC would launch a new Saturday morning preschool block programmed by PBS Kids Sprout (originally jointly owned by NBCUniversal, PBS, Sesame Workshop and Apax Partners, with the former acquiring the other's interests later that year).
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Unlike the five major commercial broadcast television networks in the United States, ABC, CBS, NBC, Fox and The CW  which compensate their affiliate stations to carry their programs  PBS is not a network but a program distributor that provides television content and related services to its member stations.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PBS" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    PBS
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  OSN News is a network of three 24-hour satellite and cable channels offering exclusively American news programming from ABC, NBC, PBS and MSNBC to U.S. expatriates and other viewers abroad, primarily geared towards an audience in the Arab countries.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MSNBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    MSNBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-12" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-12" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-12">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-12">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Orbit News is network of three 24-hour satellite and cable channels offering exclusively American news programming from ABC, NBC, PBS, and MSNBC to U.S. expatriates and other viewers abroad, primarily geared towards an audience in the Arab countries.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC_News">
                    from
                    <span>
                     NBC News
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Several ABC News programs are broadcast daily on OSN News, a service consisting of three 24-hour satellite and cable channels exclusively offering American news programs from ABC, NBC, PBS and MSNBC to U.S. expatriates and other viewers abroad, primarily geared towards an audience in the Arab countries.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ABC_News">
                    from
                    <span>
                     ABC News
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Generally, these markets had three VHF stations that were respectively affiliated with NBC, ABC and CBS (the then dominant television networks), one or more public television stations (which usually were member stations of PBS), and one or more UHF stations (and in the largest markets, such as New York City, Los Angeles and Chicago, at least one VHF station) without a network affiliation.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superstation">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Superstation
