                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-13" id="connection-excerpt-13">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     The Office
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American television comedy series that aired on NBC from March 24, 2005 to May 16, 2013. It is an adaptation of the BBC series of the same name.
                   <i>
                    The Office
                   </i>
                   was adapted for American audiences by Greg Daniels, a veteran writer for
                   <i>
                    Saturday Night Live
                   </i>
                   ,
                   <i>

                   </i>
                   , and
                   <i>
                    The
                   </i>
                   
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-13 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-13, .show-more-connection-article-13" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-13" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-13-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-13">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       The Office
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American television comedy series that aired on NBC from March 24, 2005 to May 16, 2013. It is an adaptation of the BBC series of the same name.
                     <i>
                      The Office
                     </i>
                     was adapted for American audiences by Greg Daniels, a veteran writer for
                     <i>
                      Saturday Night Live
                     </i>
                     ,
                     <i>
                      King of the Hill
                     </i>
                     , and
                     <i>
                      The Simpsons
                     </i>
                     . It is co-produced by Daniels' Deedle-Dee Productions, and Reveille Productions (later Shine America), in association with Universal Television. The original executive producers were Greg Daniels, Howard Klein, Ben Silverman, Ricky Gervais, and Stephen Merchant, with numerous others being promoted in later seasons.
                     <br/>
                     The series depicts the everyday lives of office employees in the Scranton, Pennsylvania branch of the fictional Dunder Mifflin Paper Company. To simulate the look of an actual documentary, it is filmed in a single-camera setup, without a studio audience or a laugh track. The show debuted on NBC as a mid-season replacement and ran for nine seasons, and 201 episodes.
                     <i>
                      The Office
                     </i>
                     features Steve Carell, Rainn Wilson, John Krasinski, Jenna Fischer, B. J. Novak, Ed Helms, and James Spader on the main cast. Series star Carell, who portrayed Michael Scott, left the series near the end of the seventh season.
                     <br/>
                     The first season of
                     <i>
                      The Office
                     </i>
                     was met with mixed reviews, but the following four seasons received widespread acclaim from television critics, and were included on several critics' year-end top TV series lists, winning several awards including four Primetime Emmy Awards, including Outstanding Comedy Series in 2006. Later seasons, however, were criticized for a dip in quality.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-13" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-13, #show-more-connection-article-13" href="#" id="show-less-13">

            <li class="connection" data-id="66057" data-original-title="The DuMont Television Network (also known as the DuMont Network, simply DuMont/Du Mont, or (incorrectly" data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="dumont-television-network" id="66057" title="">
             <a data-topic-id="66057" href="#!/66057/dumont-television-network">
              <ol class="post-list">
               <li>
                <div class="connection-counter">
                 14
                </div>
                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="66057" data-topic-title="DuMont Television Network" id="jTopicImage_15" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png/128px-DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png"/>
                 <div class="connection-title-and-excerpt">
                  <span class="connection-title" data-count="14" data-id="66057" data-url-title="dumont-television-network">
                   DuMont Television Network
                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   The DuMont Television Network (also known as the DuMont Network, simply DuMont/Du Mont, or (incorrectly
                  </span>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </li>
              </ol>
             </a>
            </li>
            <!-- /Collapsed connection -->
            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="66057" data-url-title="dumont-television-network" id="connection-expanded-14">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  14
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-14">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png" id="jTopicImage_15_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_15" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="66057" data-topic-title="DuMont Television Network" id="jTopicImage_15" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png/128px-DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-14">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-14" id="connection-excerpt-14">
                   The
                   <b>
                    DuMont Television Network
                   </b>
                   (also known as the
                   <b>
                    DuMont Network
                   </b>
                   , simply
                   <b>
                    DuMont
                   </b>
                   /
                   <b>
                    Du Mont
                   </b>
                   , or (incorrectly)
                   <b>
                    Dumont
                   </b>
                   <span>
                    <span>
                     /
                     <span>
                      <span>
                       d
                      </span>
                      <span>
                       u
                      </span>
                      <span>
                       m
                      </span>
                      <span>
                       
                      </span>
                      <span>
                       n
                      </span>
                      <span>
                       t
                      </span>
                     </span>
                     /
                    </span>
                   </span>
                   ) was one of the world's pioneer commercial television networks, rivalling NBC and CBS for the distinction of being first overall in the USA. It began operation in the United States in 1946. It was owned by DuMont Laboratories,
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-14 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-14, .show-more-connection-article-14" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-14" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-14-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-14">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     The
                     <b>
                      DuMont Television Network
                     </b>
                     (also known as the
                     <b>
                      DuMont Network
                     </b>
                     , simply
                     <b>
                      DuMont
                     </b>
                     /
                     <b>
                      Du Mont
                     </b>
                     , or (incorrectly)
                     <b>
                      Dumont
                     </b>
                     <span>
                      <span>
                       /
                       <span>
                        <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
                         d
                        </span>
                        <span title="/u/ long 'oo' in 'food'">
                         u
                        </span>
                        <span title="'m' in 'my'">
                         m
                        </span>
                        <span title="// short 'o' in 'body'">
                         
                        </span>
                        <span title="'n' in 'no'">
                         n
                        </span>
                        <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
                         t
                        </span>
                       </span>
                       /
                      </span>
                     </span>
                     ) was one of the world's pioneer commercial television networks, rivalling NBC and CBS for the distinction of being first overall in the USA. It began operation in the United States in 1946. It was owned by DuMont Laboratories, a television equipment and set manufacturer. The network was hindered by the prohibitive cost of broadcasting, by regulations imposed by the Federal Communications Commission (FCC) which restricted the company's growth, and even by the company's partner, Paramount Pictures. Despite several innovations in broadcasting and the creation of one of television's biggest stars of the 1950s (Jackie Gleason), the network never found itself on solid financial ground. Forced to expand on UHF channels during an era when UHF was not yet a standard feature on television sets, DuMont fought an uphill battle for program clearances outside of their three owned-and-operated stations in New York, Washington and Pittsburgh, finally ending network operations in 1956.
                     <br/>
                     DuMont's latter-day obscurity has prompted TV historian David Weinstein to refer to it as the "Forgotten Network" or "Network Is Long Gone". A few popular DuMont programs, such as
                     <i>
                      Cavalcade of Stars
                     </i>
                     and Emmy Award winner
                     <i>
                      Life Is Worth Living
                     </i>
                     , appear in television retrospectives or are mentioned briefly in books about U.S. television history, but almost all the network's programming was destroyed in the 1970s.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-14" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-14, #show-more-connection-article-14" href="#" id="show-less-14">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-14 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-14" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-14" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-14-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                DuMont Television Network
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  While rivals CBS and the DuMont Television Network also had plans to begin offering color television broadcasts, RCA convinced the FCC to approve its color system in December 1953.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Unlike CBS and NBC, which cut back on broadcasting during the war, DuMont continued full-scale experimental broadcasts throughout World War II.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DuMont_Television_Network" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    DuMont Television Network
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  The
                  <b>
                   DuMont Television Network
                  </b>
                  (also known as the
                  <b>
                   DuMont Network
                  </b>
                  , simply
                  <b>
                   DuMont
                  </b>
                  /
                  <b>
                   Du Mont
                  </b>
                  , or (incorrectly)
                  <b>
                   Dumont
                  </b>
                  ) was one of the world's pioneer commercial television networks, rivalling NBC and CBS for the distinction of being first overall in the USA.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DuMont_Television_Network" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    DuMont Television Network
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-14" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-14" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-14">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-14">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   In October 1956, NTA launched the NTA Film Network, a syndication service which distributed both films and television programs to independent television stations and stations affiliated with NBC, CBS, or ABC (DuMont had recently gone out of the network business).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NTA_Film_Network">
                    from
                    <span>
                     NTA Film Network
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   For one thing, several Mutual radio affiliates launched television stations that would often be affiliated with the television networks of ABC, CBS, DuMont, or NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutual_Broadcasting_System">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Mutual Broadcasting System
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   At the same time, rival networks NBC, ABC, and DuMont were showing interest in a Ball-Arnaz series, which Ackerman used to convince CBS to sign the duo.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I_Love_Lucy">
                    from
                    <span>
                     I Love Lucy
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Channel 11 often aired shows from CBS, DuMont and NBC that were respectively turned down by San Francisco's KPIX (channel 5) and KRON-TV (channel 4), as well as some ABC shows that also aired on KGO-TV (channel 7).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KNTV">
                    from
                    <span>
                     KNTV
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The station originally operated as a primary affiliate of the DuMont Television Network (sharing the affiliation with KBTV (channel 9, now NBC affiliate KUSA)), but also cherry-picked programs from NBC, ABC and CBS.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KWGN-TV">
                    from
                    <span>
                     KWGN-TV
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   WTMJ has been affiliated with NBC since its sign-on, owing to its radio sister's longtime affiliation with the NBC Red Network, although it also initially carried programming from CBS, ABC and DuMont.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WTMJ-TV">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WTMJ-TV
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    Mary Kay and Johnny
                   </i>
                   initially aired live on the DuMont Television Network before moving to CBS and then NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Kay_and_Johnny">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Mary Kay and Johnny
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Revue also produced later seasons of
                   <i>
                    The Jack Benny Program
                   </i>
                   for CBS and NBC and in co-operation with Jack Benny's J and M productions
                   <i>
                    Checkmate
                   </i>
                   ,
                   <i>
                    General Electric Theater
                   </i>
                   and
                   <i>
                    Alfred Hitchcock Presents
                   </i>
                   for CBS,
                   <i>
                    Studio 57
                   </i>
                   for DuMont, and westerns such as
                   <i>
                    Tales of Wells Fargo
                   </i>
                   ,
                   <i>
                    The Restless Gun
                   </i>
                   and
                   <i>
                    Laramie
                   </i>
                   for NBC, as well as
                   <i>
                    Wagon Train
                   </i>
                   for NBC and ABC, and the first two seasons of NBC's
                   <i>
                    The Virginian
                   </i>
                   , based on a film released originally by Paramount Pictures, whose pre-1950 theatrical sound feature film library was sold to MCA in 1957.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Television">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Universal Television
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Boxing From St. Nicholas Arena
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American sports program originally broadcast on NBC from 1946 to 1948, and later on the now-defunct DuMont Television Network from 1954 to 1956.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boxing_from_St._Nicholas_Arena">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Boxing from St. Nicholas Arena
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   It originally served as a primary NBC affiliate (owing to WDAF radio's longtime affiliation with the NBC Red Network) and held secondary affiliations with CBS, ABC and DuMont.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WDAF-TV">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WDAF-TV
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   From 1946 to 1956, these were ABC, CBS, NBC and DuMont (though the Paramount Television Network had some limited success during these years).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_over-the-air_television_networks">
                    from
                    <span>
                     List of United States over-the-air television networks
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Only NBC and DuMont had networks, and coaxial cable connections were only available for a few cities on the East Coast.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947%E2%80%9348_United_States_network_television_schedule">
                    from
                    <span>

                    </span>

                  </p>

               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">

                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-15">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Federal_Communications_Commission_1937_10_6.jpg" id="jTopicImage_16_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_16" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="55974" data-topic-title="U.S. Federal Communications Commission" id="jTopicImage_16" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Federal_Communications_Commission_1937_10_6.jpg/128px-Federal_Communications_Commission_1937_10_6.jpg"/>
                   <span class="copyright">

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-15">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-15" id="connection-excerpt-15">
                   The
                   <b>
                    Federal Communications Commission
                   </b>
                   (
                   <b>
                    FCC
                   </b>
                   ) is an independent agency of the United States government, created by Congressional statute (see 47 U.S.C.151 and 47 U.S.C.154) to regulate interstate communications by radio, television, wire, satellite, and cable in all 50 states, the District of Columbia and U.S. territories. The FCC works towards six
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-15 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-15, .show-more-connection-article-15" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-15" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-15-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-15">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     The
                     <b>
                      Federal Communications Commission
                     </b>
                     (
                     <b>
                      FCC
                     </b>
                     ) is an independent agency of the United States government, created by Congressional statute (see 47 U.S.C.151 and 47 U.S.C.154) to regulate interstate communications by radio, television, wire, satellite, and cable in all 50 states, the District of Columbia and U.S. territories. The FCC works towards six goals in the areas of broadband, competition, the spectrum, the media, public safety and homeland security. The Commission is also in the process of modernizing itself.
                     <br/>
                     The FCC was formed by the Communications Act of 1934 to replace the radio regulation functions of the Federal Radio Commission. The FCC took over wire communication regulation from the Interstate Commerce Commission. The FCC's mandated jurisdiction covers the 50 states, the District of Columbia, and Political divisions of the United States. The FCC also provides varied degrees of cooperation, oversight, and leadership for similar communications bodies in other countries of North America. The FCC is funded entirely by regulatory fees. It has an estimated fiscal-2011 budget of US$335.8 million and a proposed fiscal-2012 budget of $354.2 million. It has 1,720 federal employees.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-15" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-15, #show-more-connection-article-15" href="#" id="show-less-15">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-15 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-15" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-15" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-15-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                U.S. Federal Communications Commission
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  In 1934, following the government agency's creation, the Mutual Broadcasting System filed a complaint to the Federal Communications Commission (FCC), claiming it ran into difficulties trying to establish new radio stations in a market largely controlled by NBC and the Columbia Broadcasting System (CBS).
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  The major point in the report was the breakup of NBC (National Broadcasting Company), which ultimately led to the creation of ABC (American Broadcasting Company), but there were two other important points.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Federal_Communications_Commission" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    U.S. Federal Communications Commission
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  ABC began news broadcasts early in its independent existence as a radio network after the Federal Communications Commission (FCC) ordered NBC to spin off the former NBC Blue Network into an independent company in 1943.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ABC_News" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    ABC News
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-15" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-15" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-15">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-15">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   With no other applications to consider, Federal Communications Commission (FCC) approval was a mere formality, and WTVR took to the air on April 22, 1948, as the first television station south of Washington, D.C. It became an NBC affiliate June 1, 1948.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WTVR-TV">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WTVR-TV
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   In 1965, the Federal Communications Commission (FCC) reversed a 1955 station switch when NBC strong-armed Westinghouse to move to Cleveland so it could have a station in the much larger Philadelphia market.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Mike_Douglas_Show">
                    from
                    <span>
                     The Mike Douglas Show
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   On July 19, 2012, Sinclair announced that it would acquire NBC affiliate WOAI-TV (channel 4) from High Plains Broadcasting as part of its purchase of six television stations, along with the assumption of the operations of two others, from Newport Television. Since Federal Communications Commission duopoly regulations forbid common ownership of more than two full-power stations in a single market from being under the same ownership, Sinclair spun off KMYS to Deerfield Media; however, Sinclair retained control of KMYS through a shared services agreement.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KABB">
                    from
                    <span>
                     KABB
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   After Raycom acquired the Malrite Communications Group in 1999 (which owned NBC affiliate WNWO-TV), WUPW was spun off to Sunrise Television due to Federal Communications Commission (FCC) rules at the time prohibiting common ownership of two stations in the same market.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WUPW">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WUPW
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   As KYW-TV's owner, Westinghouse Broadcasting, successfully had a station swap with NBC overturned by the FCC, Westinghouse returned to Philadelphia on June 19, 1965 with call letters KYW-TV.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Douglas">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Mike Douglas
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   NBC refused to run the advertisement because of its use of the expletive, but Commoner's campaign successfully appealed to the Federal Communications Commission to allow the advertisement to run unedited.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bullshit">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Bullshit
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   In the United States, the Federal Communications Commission (FCC) settled on a color NTSC standard in 1953, and the NBC network began broadcasting a limited color television schedule in January 1954.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black-and-white">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Black-and-white
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   As a result of a 1943 Federal Communications Commission (FCC) action against anti-competitive practices, the Radio Corporation of America (RCA) was forced to sell off its broadcast subsidiary the Blue Network, the sister network of NBC, and Blue was purchased by the American Broadcasting System, Inc.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ABC_Records">
                    from
                    <span>
                     ABC Records
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Although NBC in the United States presented the entire opening ceremony from start to finish, a topless Minoan priestess was shown only briefly, the breasts having been pixelated digitally in order to avoid controversy (as the "Nipplegate" incident was still fresh in viewer's minds at the time) and potential fines by the Federal Communications Commission.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics">
                    from
                    <span>
                     2004 Summer Olympics
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                </ul>
                <a class="show-less-connection-texts less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-texts-15" data-to-show="#show-more-connection-texts-15" href="#">
                 SHOW LESS
                </a>
               </div>

            <li class="connection" data-id="5174671" data-original-title="30 Rock is an American satirical television sitcom created by Tina Fey that ran on NBC from October 11, 2006 to" data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="30-rock" id="5174671" title="">
             <a data-topic-id="5174671" href="#!/5174671/30-rock">
              <ol class="post-list">
               <li>
                <div class="connection-counter">
                 16
                </div>
                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="5174671" data-topic-title="30 Rock" id="jTopicImage_17" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                 <div class="connection-title-and-excerpt">
                  <span class="connection-title" data-count="16" data-id="5174671" data-url-title="30-rock">
                   30 Rock
                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   30 Rock is an American satirical television sitcom created by Tina Fey that ran on NBC from October 11, 2006 to
                  </span>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </li>
              </ol>
             </a>
            </li>
            <!-- /Collapsed connection -->
            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="5174671" data-url-title="30-rock" id="connection-expanded-16">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  16
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-16">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_17_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_17" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="5174671" data-topic-title="30 Rock" id="jTopicImage_17" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-16">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-16" id="connection-excerpt-16">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     30 Rock
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American satirical television sitcom created by Tina Fey that ran on NBC from October 11, 2006 to January 31, 2013. The series, loosely based on Fey's experiences as head writer for
                   <i>
                    Saturday Night Live
                   </i>
                   , takes place behind the scenes of a fictional live sketch comedy show depicted as airing on NBC.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-16 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-16, .show-more-connection-article-16" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-16" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-16-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-16">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       30 Rock
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American satirical television sitcom created by Tina Fey that ran on NBC from October 11, 2006 to January 31, 2013. The series, loosely based on Fey's experiences as head writer for
                     <i>
                      Saturday Night Live
                     </i>
                     , takes place behind the scenes of a fictional live sketch comedy show depicted as airing on NBC. The series' name refers to 30 Rockefeller Plaza in New York City, the address of the GE Building, in which the NBC Studios are located. This series is produced by Broadway Video and Little Stranger, Inc., in association with NBCUniversal.
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      30 Rock
                     </i>
                     episodes were produced in a single-camera setup (with the exception of the two live episodes that were taped in the multi-camera format), and were filmed in New York. The pilot episode premiered on October 11, 2006, and seven seasons followed. The series stars Fey with a supporting cast that includes Alec Baldwin, Tracy Morgan, Jane Krakowski, Jack McBrayer, Scott Adsit, Judah Friedlander, Katrina Bowden, Keith Powell, Lonny Ross, John Lutz, Kevin Brown, Grizz Chapman, Maulik Pancholy and Rachel Dratch.
                     <br/>
                     Tonally,
                     <i>
                      30 Rock
                     </i>
                     uses absurdist humor to parody the complex corporate structure of NBC and its then parent company General Electric. Television critic Todd VanDerWerff
                     <i>
                      The A.V. Club
                     </i>
                     once remarked that it 'usually adopts the manic pacing of a live-action cartoon.' The show was influential in its extensive use of smash cuts: sudden, short cuts to unrelated scenes showing something the characters are briefly discussing.
                     <i>
                      30 Rock
                     </i>
                     also became known for its dedication to making these extremely elaborate, once showing a set that took three days to build for only six seconds of video.
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      30 Rock
                     </i>
                     was a runaway critical success, winning several major awards (including Primetime Emmy Awards for Outstanding Comedy Series in 2007, 2008, and 2009 and nominations for every other year it ran), and achieving the esteemed top ranking on a myriad critics' year-end best of 2006-2013 lists. On July 14, 2009, the series was nominated for 22 Primetime Emmy Awards, the most in a single year for a comedy series. Over the course of the series, it was nominated for 112 Emmy awards and won 16, in addition to numerous other nominations and wins from other awards shows. Despite the acclaim, the series struggled in the ratings throughout its run, something which Fey herself has made light of.
                     <br/>
                     In 2009, Comedy Central and WGN America bought the syndication rights to the show, which began airing on both networks on September 19, 2011; the series also entered into local broadcast syndication on the same day. Today,
                     <i>
                      30 Rock
                     </i>
                     is regarded as a landmark series. Its series finale in particular has been named as one of the greatest in television history by several publications. In 2013, the Writers Guild of America named
                     <i>
                      30 Rock
                     </i>
                     the 21st best-written television series of all time.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-16" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-16, #show-more-connection-article-16" href="#" id="show-less-16">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-17">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-17" id="connection-excerpt-17">
                   <b>
                    Ion Television
                   </b>
                   is an American broadcast, cable, satellite and digital television network that is owned by Ion Media Networks. The network first began broadcasting on August 31, 1998 as
                   <b>
                    Pax TV
                   </b>
                   , focusing primarily on family-oriented entertainment programming; it rebranded as
                   <b>
                    i: Independent Television
                   </b>
                   on June 28, 2005, converting into a general entertainment network featuring mainly recent and older acquired programs; the network adopted its current identity as Ion Television on January 29, 2007.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-17 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-17, .show-more-connection-article-17" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-17" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-17-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-17">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Ion Television
                     </b>
                     is an American broadcast, cable, satellite and digital television network that is owned by Ion Media Networks. The network first began broadcasting on August 31, 1998 as
                     <b>
                      Pax TV
                     </b>
                     , focusing primarily on family-oriented entertainment programming; it rebranded as
                     <b>
                      i: Independent Television
                     </b>
                     on June 28, 2005, converting into a general entertainment network featuring mainly recent and older acquired programs; the network adopted its current identity as Ion Television on January 29, 2007.
                     <br/>
                     As of 2013, Ion Television is receivable to approximately 101,373,000 television households in the United States through its group of 60+ stations, as well as through distribution on cable and satellite providers (which serve as the network's sole method of distribution in markets where Ion does not have an owned-and-operated station or affiliate). The network's stations cover all of the top 20 U.S. markets and 37 of the top 50 markets.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-17" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-17, #show-more-connection-article-17" href="#" id="show-less-17">

                   </a>

            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="303749" data-url-title="comcast" id="connection-expanded-18">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  18
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-18">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_19_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_19" data-searched="" data-topic-id="303749" data-topic-title="Comcast" id="jTopicImage_19" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-18">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-18" id="connection-excerpt-18">
                   <b>
                    Comcast Corporation
                   </b>
                   , formerly registered as
                   <b>
                    Comcast Holdings
                   </b>
                   , is a U.S.-based multinational mass media company and is the largest broadcasting and cable company in the world by revenue. It is the largest cable company and home Internet service provider in the United States, and the nation's third largest home telephone service provider. Comcast services U.S. residential and commercial customers in 40 states and the District of Columbia. The company's headquarters is located in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-18 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-18, .show-more-connection-article-18" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-18" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-18-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-18">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Comcast Corporation
                     </b>
                     , formerly registered as
                     <b>
                      Comcast Holdings
                     </b>
                     , is a U.S.-based multinational mass media company and is the largest broadcasting and cable company in the world by revenue. It is the largest cable company and home Internet service provider in the United States, and the nation's third largest home telephone service provider. Comcast services U.S. residential and commercial customers in 40 states and the District of Columbia. The company's headquarters is located in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania.
                     <br/>
                     As the owner of the international media company NBCUniversal since 2011, Comcast is a producer of feature films and television programs intended for theatrical exhibition and over-the-air and cable television broadcast.
                     <br/>
                     Comcast operates multiple cable-only channels (including E! Entertainment Television, the Golf Channel, and NBCSN), over-the-air national broadcast network channels (NBC and Telemundo), the film production studio Universal Pictures, and Universal Parks &amp; Resorts, with a global total of nearly 200 family entertainment locations and attractions in the U.S. and several other countries including U.A.E., South Korea, Russia and China, with several new locations reportedly planned and being developed for future operation. Comcast also has significant holding in digital distribution (ThePlatform). In February 2014 the company agreed to merge with Time Warner Cable in an equity swap deal worth $45.2 billion. Under the terms of the agreement Comcast was to acquire 100% of Time Warner Cable.  However, on April 24, 2015, Comcast terminated the agreement.
                     <br/>
                     Comcast has been criticized for multiple reasons. The company's customer satisfaction often ranks among the lowest in the cable industry. Comcast has violated net neutrality practices in the past; and, despite Comcast's commitment to a narrow definition of net neutrality, critics advocate a definition of which precludes distinction between Comcast's private network services and the rest of the Internet. Critics also point out a lack of competition; in the vast majority of Comcast's service area, it does not compete with other cable providers. Given Comcast's negotiating power as a large ISP, some suspect that Comcast could leverage paid peering agreements to unfairly influence end-user connection speeds. These issues, in addition to others, led to Comcast being dubbed "The Worst Company in America" by
                     <i>
                      The Consumerist
                     </i>
                     in 2014.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-18" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-18, #show-more-connection-article-18" href="#" id="show-less-18">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-19">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-19" id="connection-excerpt-19">
                   <b>
                    NBCUniversal, Inc.
                   </b>
                    formerly known as
                   <b>
                    NBCUniversal Media, LLC
                   </b>
                   since January 29, 2011,
                   <b>
                    NBC Universal, Inc.
                   </b>
                   from November 28, 2004 to January 28, 2011 (after the merger of National Broadcasting Company &amp; Vivendi Universal Entertainment), &amp;
                   <b>
                    National Broadcasting Company, Inc.
                   </b>
                   from April 30, 1939 to November 27, 2004 and colloquially referred to as
                   <b>
                    NBCU
                   </b>
                   or
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-19 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-19, .show-more-connection-article-19" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-19" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-19-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-19">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      NBCUniversal, Inc.
                     </b>
                      formerly known as
                     <b>
                      NBCUniversal Media, LLC
                     </b>
                     since January 29, 2011,
                     <b>
                      NBC Universal, Inc.
                     </b>
                     from November 28, 2004 to January 28, 2011 (after the merger of National Broadcasting Company &amp; Vivendi Universal Entertainment), &amp;
                     <b>
                      National Broadcasting Company, Inc.
                     </b>
                     from April 30, 1939 to November 27, 2004 and colloquially referred to as
                     <b>
                      NBCU
                     </b>
                     or
                     <b>
                      NBCUni
                     </b>
                      is an American media and entertainment company engaged in the production and marketing of entertainment, news, and information products and services to a global customer base. The company owns and operates American television networks, numerous cable channels, and a group of local stations in the United States, as well as motion picture companies, several television production companies, and branded theme parks. It is the world's largest mass media group.
                     <br/>
                     NBC Universal was formed in April 2004 by the merger of General Electric's National Broadcasting Company with Vivendi's Vivendi Universal Entertainment. GE and US cable TV operator Comcast announced a buyout agreement for the company on December 3, 2009. Following regulatory approvals, the transaction completed on January 28, 2011. Comcast subsequently owned 51% of NBCUniversal while GE owned 49%. Comcast intended to buy out the rest of GE's stake over the following seven years, but nothing happened until February 12, 2013, when Comcast announced its intention to complete the purchase all at once and assume 100% ownership of the company by the end of March. The deal was finalized on March 19, 2013.
                     <br/>
                     Originally, the NBC Universal logo was a combination of the NBC peacock logo and the Universal Studios globe and text. The logo was redesigned by Wolff Olins in January 2011 to reflect the new Comcast ownership and the unity of its two main divisions.
                     <br/>
                     NBCUniversal is headquartered in Rockefeller Plaza's Comcast Building (formerly the GE Building) in Midtown Manhattan, New York City. The company is one of two successor companies to MCA Inc. (Music Corporation of America), the other being Vivendi through its subsidiary Universal Music Group.
                    </p>

                <li>

                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-20">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_21_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_21" data-searched="" data-topic-id="1196887" data-topic-title="WNBC" id="jTopicImage_21" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-20">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-20" id="connection-excerpt-20">
                   <b>
                    WNBC
                   </b>
                   , channel 4, is the flagship station of the NBC Television Network, located in New York City. WNBC is owned by the NBCUniversal Owned Television Stations group, and operates as part of a television duopoly with Linden, New Jersey-licensed Telemundo owned-and-operated station WNJU (channel 47); both are owned by Comcast subsidiary NBCUniversal, which also holds a minority stake in regional sports network SportsNet New York.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-20 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-20, .show-more-connection-article-20" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-20" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-20-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-20">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      WNBC
                     </b>
                     , channel 4, is the flagship station of the NBC Television Network, located in New York City. WNBC is owned by the NBCUniversal Owned Television Stations group, and operates as part of a television duopoly with Linden, New Jersey-licensed Telemundo owned-and-operated station WNJU (channel 47); both are owned by Comcast subsidiary NBCUniversal, which also holds a minority stake in regional sports network SportsNet New York.
                     <br/>
                     WNBC's studios are co-located with NBC's corporate headquarters at 30 Rockefeller Plaza in midtown Manhattan, and its transmitter is based at the Empire State Building. The station is the oldest fully licensed television station in continuous operation in the United States.
                     <br/>
                     In the few areas of the eastern United States where an NBC station is not receivable over-the-air, WNBC is available on satellite via DirecTV and Dish Network (the latter carries the station as part of All American Direct's distant network package), which also provides coverage of the station to Latin American and Caribbean countries. It is also carried on certain cable providers in markets where an NBC affiliate is not available, on LiveTV and Dish Network. DirecTV also allows subscribers in the Los Angeles market to receive WNBC for an additional monthly fee.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-20" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-20, #show-more-connection-article-20" href="#" id="show-less-20">

                   </a>
                  </div>

            <li class="connection" data-id="7587" data-original-title="Cable television is a system of delivering television programming to paying subscribers via radio frequency (RF)" data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="cable-television" id="7587" title="">
             <a data-topic-id="7587" href="#!/7587/cable-television">
              <ol class="post-list">
               <li>
                <div class="connection-counter">
                 21
                </div>
                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="7587" data-topic-title="Cable television" id="jTopicImage_22" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/F-Stecker_und_Kabel.jpg/128px-F-Stecker_und_Kabel.jpg"/>
                 <div class="connection-title-and-excerpt">
                  <span class="connection-title" data-count="21" data-id="7587" data-url-title="cable-television">
                   Cable television
                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   Cable television is a system of delivering television programming to paying subscribers via radio frequency (RF)
                  </span>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </li>
              </ol>
             </a>
            </li>
            <!-- /Collapsed connection -->
            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="7587" data-url-title="cable-television" id="connection-expanded-21">
             <div class="connection-scroll">

               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  21
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-21">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:F-Stecker_und_Kabel.jpg" id="jTopicImage_22_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_22" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="7587" data-topic-title="Cable television" id="jTopicImage_22" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/F-Stecker_und_Kabel.jpg/128px-F-Stecker_und_Kabel.jpg"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-21">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-21" id="connection-excerpt-21">
                   <b>
                    Cable television
                   </b>
                   is a system of delivering television programming to paying subscribers via radio frequency (RF) signals transmitted through coaxial cables or light pulses through fiber-optic cables. This contrasts with broadcast television, in which the television signal is transmitted over the air by radio waves and received by a television antenna attached to the television. FM radio programming, high-speed Internet, telephone service, and similar non-television services may also be provided through these cables.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-21 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-21, .show-more-connection-article-21" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-21" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-21-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-21">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Cable television
                     </b>
                     is a system of delivering television programming to paying subscribers via radio frequency (RF) signals transmitted through coaxial cables or light pulses through fiber-optic cables. This contrasts with broadcast television, in which the television signal is transmitted over the air by radio waves and received by a television antenna attached to the television. FM radio programming, high-speed Internet, telephone service, and similar non-television services may also be provided through these cables.
                     <br/>
                     The abbreviation
                     <b>
                      CATV
                     </b>
                     is often used for cable television. It originally stood for
                     <i>
                      Community Access Television
                     </i>
                     or
                     <i>
                      Community Antenna Television
                     </i>
                     , from cable television's origins in 1948: in areas where over-the-air reception was limited by distance from transmitters or mountainous terrain, large "community antennas" were constructed, and cable was run from them to individual homes. The origins of cable
                     <i>
                      broadcasting
                     </i>
                     are even older as radio programming was distributed by cable in some European cities as far back as 1924.
                     <br/>
                     Earlier cable television was analog, but since 2000s all cable operators have switched to or are in process of switching to digital cable television.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-21" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-21, #show-more-connection-article-21" href="#" id="show-less-21">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-21 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-21" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-21" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-21-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->

                 <p>
                  As cable television franchises began to be incorporated around the United States during the 1960s and 1970s, independent stations from large and mid-sized markets were imported by these systems via wire or microwave relay to smaller media markets, which often only had stations that were affiliated with the Big Three television networks (ABC, NBC and CBS); these independents became the first "superstations," which were distributed on a statewide or regional basis.

             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">

                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-22">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Seinfeld_actors_montage.jpg" id="jTopicImage_23_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_23" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="28606" data-topic-title="Seinfeld" id="jTopicImage_23" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Seinfeld_actors_montage.jpg/128px-Seinfeld_actors_montage.jpg"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-22">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-22" id="connection-excerpt-22">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Seinfeld
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American television sitcom that originally ran for nine seasons on NBC from July 5, 1989, to May 14, 1998. It was created by Larry David and Jerry Seinfeld, the latter starring as a fictionalized version of himself. Set predominantly in an apartment block in Manhattan's Upper West Side in New York City,
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-22 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-22, .show-more-connection-article-22" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-22" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-22-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-22">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Seinfeld
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American television sitcom that originally ran for nine seasons on NBC from July 5, 1989, to May 14, 1998. It was created by Larry David and Jerry Seinfeld, the latter starring as a fictionalized version of himself. Set predominantly in an apartment block in Manhattan's Upper West Side in New York City, the show features a handful of Jerry's friends and acquaintances, particularly best friend George Costanza (Jason Alexander), former girlfriend Elaine Benes (Julia Louis-Dreyfus), and neighbor across the hall Cosmo Kramer (Michael Richards).
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      Seinfeld
                     </i>
                     was produced by Castle Rock Entertainment. In syndication the series has been distributed by Sony Pictures Television since 2002. It was largely co-written by David and Seinfeld with script writers, who included Larry Charles, Peter Mehlman, Gregg Kavet, Andy Robin, Carol Leifer, David Mandel, Jeff Schaffer, Steve Koren, Jennifer Crittenden, Tom Gammill, Max Pross, Dan O'Keefe, Charlie Rubin, Marjorie Gross, Alec Berg, Elaine Pope, and Spike Feresten.
                     <br/>
                     A favorite among critics, the show led the Nielsen ratings in seasons six and nine, and finished among the top two (with NBC's
                     <i>
                      ER
                     </i>
                     ) every year from 1994 to 1998. In 2002,
                     <i>
                      TV Guide
                     </i>
                     named
                     <i>
                      Seinfeld
                     </i>
                     the greatest television program of all time. In 1997, the episodes "The Boyfriend" and "The Parking Garage" were respectively ranked numbers 4 and 33 on
                     <i>
                      TV Guide'
                     </i>
                     s 100 Greatest Episodes of All Time, and in 2009, "The Contest" was ranked #1 on the same magazine's list of TV's Top 100 Episodes of All Time. E! named it the "number 1 reason the '90s ruled." In 2013, the Writers Guild of America named
                     <i>
                      Seinfeld
                     </i>
                     the No. 2 Best Written TV Series of All Time (second to
                     <i>
                      The Sopranos
                     </i>
                     ). That same year,
                     <i>
                      Entertainment Weekly
                     </i>
                     named it the No. 3 best TV series of all time.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-22" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-22, #show-more-connection-article-22" href="#" id="show-less-22">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                SHOW MORE
               </a>

                 <div class="connection-counter">
