                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-23">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dayparts.png" id="jTopicImage_24_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_24" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="24973" data-topic-title="Prime time" id="jTopicImage_24" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Dayparts.png/128px-Dayparts.png"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-23">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-23" id="connection-excerpt-23">
                   <b>
                    Prime time
                   </b>
                   or
                   <b>
                    peak time
                   </b>
                   is the block of broadcast programming taking place during the middle of the evening for television programming.
                   <br/>
                   The term
                   <i>
                    prime time
                   </i>
                   is often defined in terms of a fixed time period  for example, from 19:00 to 22:00 (Central and Mountain Time) or 20:00 to 23:00 (Eastern and Pacific Time) (7 p.m. to 10 p.m. or 8 p.m. to 11 p.m.).
                  </p>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-23">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-23" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-23, #show-more-connection-article-23" href="#" id="show-less-23">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Prime time
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  By 1963, much of NBC's prime time schedule was presented in color, although some popular series (such as
                  <i>
                   The Man from U.N.C.L.E.
                  </i>
                  , which premiered in late 1964) were broadcast in black-and-white for their entire first season.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  In the 1987-1988 season, NBC-owned stations in several cities experimented with airing a schedule of syndicated first-run sitcoms at 7:30/6:30p.m. (known as ) to compete against syndicated reruns or game shows such as
                  <i>
                   Wheel of Fortune
                  </i>
                  on rival stations.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_time" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Prime time
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  This does not necessarily apply universally; in 2001, after an XFL game went into overtime, forcing the delay of a highly promoted episode of
                  <i>
                   Saturday Night Live
                  </i>
                  , NBC made a decision to cut off all future XFL broadcasts at 11:00p.m.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_time" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Prime time
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-23" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-23" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-23">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-23">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Since the "Heidi Game" incident in 1968, in which NBC cut away on the East Coast from a New York Jets/Oakland Raiders football game in its final minute of play in order to show a movie (and, in the process, missing an unexpected comeback by the Raiders to win the game), the National Football League began to mandate that all games be broadcast in their entirety.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_time">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Prime time
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Just as notable were CBS's news segments for children,
                   <i>
                    In the News
                   </i>
                   and NBC's
                   <i>
                    Ask NBC News
                   </i>
                   and
                   <i>
                    One to Grow On
                   </i>
                   , which featured skits of everyday problems with advice from the stars of NBC primetime programs.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturday-morning_cartoon">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Saturday-morning cartoon
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   As a VHF station competitor, KTVU aired
                   <i>
                    The 8 O'Clock Movie
                   </i>
                   as an alternative to network programs that aired during prime time on NBC affiliate KRON-TV (channel 4, now a MyNetworkTV affiliate), CBS affiliate KPIX (channel 5, now an owned-and-operated station of that network) and ABC owned-and-operated station KGO-TV (channel 7).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KTVU">
                    from
                    <span>
                     KTVU
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     The Flintstone Primetime Specials (also known as "The Flintstone Special")
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is a limited-run animated cartoon revival of the 1960s series original,
                   <i>
                    The Flintstones
                   </i>
                   produced by Hanna-Barbera Productions, premiered on NBC in primetime and ran from September 26, 1980 to October 11, 1981.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Flintstone_Primetime_Specials">
                    from
                    <span>
                     The Flintstone Primetime Specials
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Occasionally as time permits, KICU may air Fox network programs whenever KTVU is unable to in the event that channel 2 must air extended breaking news coverage or because of conflicts with other locally produced special programming on that station; this was also the case when KTVU aired San Francisco Giants baseball games that ran into or aired during primetime hours, until it lost the broadcast television rights to the Giants to NBC owned-and-operated station KNTV (channel 11) in 2007.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KICU-TV">
                    from
                    <span>
                     KICU-TV
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Jimmy Powers took over the role in 1949 and remained NBC's main boxing announcer until the network ceased carrying prime time boxing matches in 1960.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gillette_Cavalcade_of_Sports">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Gillette Cavalcade of Sports
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Hill Street Blues
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American serial police drama that was first aired on NBC in 1981 and ran for 146 episodes on primetime into 1987.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hill_Street_Blues">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Hill Street Blues
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   NBC, which had the broadcast rights to the games, partnered with Cablevision for the experiment, believing that people would pay between $95 to $170 to see events live that would normally be shown on tape delay on the network in prime time.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olympics_on_television">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Olympics on television
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   NBC, which had broadcast rights to the Games, thought that viewers would be willing to pay $95 to $170 to see events live, which would normally be shown on tape delay on the network in prime time.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olympics_Triplecast">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Olympics Triplecast
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Sponsored by Unilever's blue detergent, Surf, the program began as a one hour comedy-drama on June 17, 1950, and ran in prime time on the NBC network until October 12, 1950.

                    </span>

                  </p>

                    <span>

                    </span>

                  </p>

                   is an American musical variety television series starring singer Eddie Fisher which was broadcast by NBC on Wednesday nights in early prime time from 1953 to 1957.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coke_Time_with_Eddie_Fisher">

                    <span>

            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="174220" data-url-title="gunsmoke" id="connection-expanded-24">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  24
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-24">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:James_Arness_Matt_Dillon_Gunsmoke_1969.JPG" id="jTopicImage_25_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_25" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="174220" data-topic-title="Gunsmoke" id="jTopicImage_25" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/James_Arness_Matt_Dillon_Gunsmoke_1969.JPG/128px-James_Arness_Matt_Dillon_Gunsmoke_1969.JPG"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-24">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-24" id="connection-excerpt-24">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Gunsmoke
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American radio and television Western drama series created by director Norman Macdonnell and writer John Meston. The stories take place in and around Dodge City, Kansas, during the settlement of the American West. The central character is lawman Marshal Matt Dillon, played by William Conrad on radio and James Arness on television. When aired in the UK, the television series was initially titled
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Gun Law
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   , later reverting to
                   <i>
                    Gunsmoke
                   </i>
                   .
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-24 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-24, .show-more-connection-article-24" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-24" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-24-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-24">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Gunsmoke
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American radio and television Western drama series created by director Norman Macdonnell and writer John Meston. The stories take place in and around Dodge City, Kansas, during the settlement of the American West. The central character is lawman Marshal Matt Dillon, played by William Conrad on radio and James Arness on television. When aired in the UK, the television series was initially titled
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Gun Law
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     , later reverting to
                     <i>
                      Gunsmoke
                     </i>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     The radio series ran from 1952 to 1961. John Dunning wrote that among radio drama enthusiasts, "
                     <i>
                      Gunsmoke
                     </i>
                     is routinely placed among the best shows of any kind and any time." The television series ran for 20 seasons from 1955 to 1975, and stands as the United States' longest-running prime time, live-action drama with 635 episodes. In 2010,
                     <i>
                      Law &amp; Order
                     </i>
                     tied
                     <i>
                      Gunsmoke
                     </i>
                     for most seasons for a live action drama series when it finished its twentieth and final season, but the show finished 179 episodes short of
                     <i>
                      Gunsmoke'
                     </i>
                     s final total; in terms of prime-time scripted series with continuing characters,
                     <i>
                      The Simpsons
                     </i>
                     is the only program to exceed 20 seasons. At the end of its run in 1975,
                     <i>
                      Los Angeles Times
                     </i>
                     columnist Cecil Smith wrote: "
                     <i>
                      Gunsmoke
                     </i>
                     was the dramatization of the American epic legend of the west. Our own
                     <i>
                      Iliad
                     </i>
                     and
                     <i>
                      Odyssey
                     </i>
                     , created from standard elements of the dime novel and the pulp western as romanticized by [Ned] Buntline, [Bret] Harte, and [Mark] Twain. It was ever the stuff of legend."
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-24" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-24, #show-more-connection-article-24" href="#" id="show-less-24">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-24 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-24" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-24" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-24-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                   Days of Our Lives
                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   Days of Our Lives (also stylized as Days of our Lives; often abbreviated to DOOL or Days) is an American daytime
                  </span>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </li>

             </a>
            </li>

               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">

                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-25">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_26_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_26" data-searched="" data-topic-id="32001841" data-topic-title="Days of Our Lives" id="jTopicImage_26" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-25">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-25" id="connection-excerpt-25">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Days of Our Lives
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   (also stylized as
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Days of our Lives
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   ; often abbreviated to
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     DOOL
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   or
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Days
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   ) is an American daytime soap opera broadcast on the NBC television network. It is one of the longest-running scripted television programs in the world, airing nearly every weekday since November 8, 1965. It has since been syndicated to
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-25 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-25, .show-more-connection-article-25" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-25" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-25-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-25">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Days of Our Lives
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     (also stylized as
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Days of our Lives
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     ; often abbreviated to
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       DOOL
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     or
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Days
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     ) is an American daytime soap opera broadcast on the NBC television network. It is one of the longest-running scripted television programs in the world, airing nearly every weekday since November 8, 1965. It has since been syndicated to many countries around the world. It rebroadcast same-day episodes on SOAPnet weeknights at 8 and 10 p.m. (ET/PT) until the network's closure in 2013. The series was created by husband-and-wife team Ted Corday and Betty Corday. Irna Phillips was a story editor for
                     <i>
                      Days of Our Lives
                     </i>
                     and many of the show's earliest storylines were written by William J. Bell. In January 2014, the show was renewed through September 2016.
                     <br/>
                     Due to the series' success, it was expanded from 30 minutes to 60 minutes on April 21, 1975. Since that date, the mid-show bumper, featuring the phrase "We will return for the second half of
                     <i>
                      Days of Our Lives
                     </i>
                     in just a moment", was aired with every episode and voiced by the series' original star, Macdonald Carey. The series focuses on its core families, the Hortons and the Bradys. Several other families have been added to the cast, and many of them still appear on the show. Frances Reid, the matriarch of the series' Horton family remained with the show from its inception to her death on February 3, 2010. Suzanne Rogers celebrated 40 years on
                     <i>
                      Days of Our Lives
                     </i>
                     this year, appearing on the show more or less since her first appearance in 1973. Susan Seaforth Hayes is the only cast member to appear on
                     <i>
                      Days of Our Lives
                     </i>
                     in all five decades it has been on air.
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      Days of Our Lives
                     </i>
                     aired its 10,000th episode on February 21, 2005 and its 12,000th episode aired on January 11, 2013. The show was given the title of most daring drama in the seventies due to covering topics other soaps would not dare to do. The show's executive producer is Ken Corday, and co-executive producers are Greg Meng and Lisa de Cazotte.
                     <i>
                      Days of Our Lives
                     </i>
                     is the most widely distributed soap opera in the United States. The original title sequence voiced by MacDonald Carey is still used to this day.
                     <br/>
                     The show has been parodied by SCTV (as "The Days of the Week") and the television sitcom
                     <i>
                      Friends
                     </i>
                     , with some cast members making crossover appearances on the show, including Kristian Alfonso, Roark Critchlow, Matthew Ashford, Kyle Lowder, and Alison Sweeney. The show has high-profile fans such as actress Julia Roberts, and the late Supreme Court justice Thurgood Marshall.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-25" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-25, #show-more-connection-article-25" href="#" id="show-less-25">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>

                SHOW MORE

             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  26
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-26">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_27_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_27" data-searched="" data-topic-id="21998954" data-topic-title="Community (TV series)" id="jTopicImage_27" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-26">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-26" id="connection-excerpt-26">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Community
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American television sitcom created by Dan Harmon that premiered on NBC on September 17, 2009. The single-camera series follows an ensemble cast of students at a community college in the fictional town of Greendale, Colorado. It makes heavy use of meta-humor and pop culture references, often parodying film and television clichs and tropes.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-26 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-26, .show-more-connection-article-26" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-26" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-26-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-26">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Community
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American television sitcom created by Dan Harmon that premiered on NBC on September 17, 2009. The single-camera series follows an ensemble cast of students at a community college in the fictional town of Greendale, Colorado. It makes heavy use of meta-humor and pop culture references, often parodying film and television clichs and tropes.
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      Community
                     </i>
                     has received acclaim from critics, being ranked in several critics' lists of the best television series in 2010, 2011, and 2012, and has gained a cult following. Following cancellation by NBC in May 2014 after five seasons,
                     <i>
                      Community
                     </i>
                     was renewed for a sixth, 13-episode season by Yahoo! Screen, which ran from March 17 to June 2, 2015.
                    </p>
                   </div>

               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  27
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-27">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wheel_of_Fortune_Round_1_template_Season_31.png" id="jTopicImage_28_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_28" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="25749059" data-topic-title="Wheel of Fortune (U.S. game show)" id="jTopicImage_28" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Wheel_of_Fortune_Round_1_template_Season_31.png/128px-Wheel_of_Fortune_Round_1_template_Season_31.png"/>
                   <span class="copyright">

                  </a>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-27">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-27" id="connection-excerpt-27">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Wheel of Fortune
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   (often known simply as
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Wheel
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   ) is an American television game show created by Merv Griffin. The show features a competition in which contestants solve word puzzles, similar to those used in Hangman, to win cash and prizes determined by spinning a giant carnival wheel.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-27 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-27, .show-more-connection-article-27" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-27" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-27-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-27">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Wheel of Fortune
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     (often known simply as
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Wheel
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     ) is an American television game show created by Merv Griffin. The show features a competition in which contestants solve word puzzles, similar to those used in Hangman, to win cash and prizes determined by spinning a giant carnival wheel.
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      Wheel
                     </i>
                     premiered as a daytime series on NBC on January 6, 1975, and continued to air on the network until June 30, 1989. After some changes were made to its format, the daytime series returned on July 17, 1989 as part of CBS' daytime lineup. On January 14, 1991,
                     <i>
                      Wheel
                     </i>
                     moved back to NBC and aired on that network until it was cancelled on September 20, 1991. The popularity of the daytime series led to a nightly syndicated edition being developed; that series premiered on September 19, 1983 and continues to air to this day.
                     <br/>
                     The network version was originally hosted by Chuck Woolery and Susan Stafford, with Charlie O'Donnell as its announcer. O'Donnell left in 1980, Woolery in 1981, and Stafford in 1982; they were replaced, respectively, by Jack Clark, Pat Sajak, and Vanna White. After Clark's death in 1988, M. G. Kelly took over briefly as announcer until O'Donnell returned in 1989; O'Donnell remained on the network version until its cancellation, and continued to announce on the syndicated show until his death in 2010, after which he was replaced by Jim Thornton, who has been the announcer since. Sajak left the network version in January 1989 to host his own late-night talk show, and was replaced on that version by Rolf Benirschke. Bob Goen replaced Benirschke when the network show moved to CBS, then remained as host until the network show was canceled altogether. The syndicated version has been hosted continuously by Sajak and White since its inception.
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      Wheel of Fortune
                     </i>
                     ranks as the longest-running syndicated game show in the United States, with over 6,000 episodes aired.
                     <i>
                      TV Guide
                     </i>
                     named it the "top-rated syndicated series" in a 2008 article, and in 2013, the magazine ranked it at #2 in its list of the 60 greatest game shows ever. The program has also come to gain a worldwide following with sixty international adaptations. The syndicated series' 32nd season premiered on September 15, 2014.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-27" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-27, #show-more-connection-article-27" href="#" id="show-less-27">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-27 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-27" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-27" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-27-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-28">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-28" id="connection-excerpt-28">
                   <b>
                    Universal Television
                   </b>
                   is the television production subsidiary of the NBCUniversal Television Group and, by extension, the production arm of the NBC television network (since a majority of the company's shows air on NBC, and accounts for most of that network's prime time programming). It was formerly known as
                   <b>
                    Revue Studios
                   </b>
                   ,
                   <b>
                    MCA/Universal
                   </b>
                   ,
                   <b>
                    NBC Studios
                   </b>
                   ,
                   <b>
                    NBC Universal
                   </b>
                   
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-28 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-28, .show-more-connection-article-28" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-28" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-28-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-28">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Universal Television
                     </b>
                     is the television production subsidiary of the NBCUniversal Television Group and, by extension, the production arm of the NBC television network (since a majority of the company's shows air on NBC, and accounts for most of that network's prime time programming). It was formerly known as
                     <b>
                      Revue Studios
                     </b>
                     ,
                     <b>
                      MCA/Universal
                     </b>
                     ,
                     <b>
                      NBC Studios
                     </b>
                     ,
                     <b>
                      NBC Universal Television Studio
                     </b>
                     , and
                     <b>
                      Universal Media Studios
                     </b>
                     . Both NBC Studios and Universal Network Television are predecessors of Universal Media Studios.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-28" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-28, #show-more-connection-article-28" href="#" id="show-less-28">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>

               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Universal Television
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  <b>
                   NBC Productions
                  </b>
                  was founded in 1947 by RCA (NBC's former parent company).
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Television" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Universal Television
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Revue also produced later seasons of
                  <i>
                   The Jack Benny Program
                  </i>
                  for CBS and NBC and in co-operation with Jack Benny's J and M productions
                  <i>
                   Checkmate
                  </i>
                  ,
                  <i>
                   General Electric Theater
                  </i>
                  and
                  <i>
                   Alfred Hitchcock Presents
                  </i>
                  for CBS,
                  <i>
                   Studio 57
                  </i>
                  for DuMont, and westerns such as
                  <i>
                   Tales of Wells Fargo
                  </i>
                  ,
                  <i>
                   The Restless Gun
                  </i>
                  and
                  <i>
                   Laramie
                  </i>
                  for NBC, as well as
                  <i>
                   Wagon Train
                  </i>
                  for NBC and ABC, and the first two seasons of NBC's
                  <i>
                   The Virginian
                  </i>
                  , based on a film released originally by Paramount Pictures, whose pre-1950 theatrical sound feature film library was sold to MCA in 1957.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Television" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Universal Television
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  <b>
                   Universal Television
                  </b>
                  is the television production subsidiary of the NBCUniversal Television Group and, by extension, the production arm of the NBC television network (since a majority of the company's shows air on NBC, and accounts for most of that network's prime time programming).
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Television" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Universal Television
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-28" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-28" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-28">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-28">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Many of its series were produced in association with Universal Television; most of them aired on the NBC television network in the U.S.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_VII_Limited">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Mark VII Limited
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   He was executive producer and house director for the NBC series
                   <i>
                    The Event
                   </i>
                   under his deal with Universal Media Studios during the show's 20102011 run.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Reiner">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Jeffrey Reiner
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   On July 30, 2009, it was revealed that NBC, Universal Media Studios and Steve Carell's Carousel Television, were teaming up to produce a revival of the show.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Rockford_Files">
                    from
                    <span>
                     The Rockford Files
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   It is based on the John Jeffcoat film of the same name and adapted by Robert Borden of George Lopez and Universal Media Studios for NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outsourced_%28TV_series%29">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Outsourced (TV series)
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The program aired on NBC and was packaged by Jack Webb's Mark VII Limited for Universal Television.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sierra_%28TV_series%29">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Sierra (TV series)
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>

                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Parenthood
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American television drama series developed by Jason Katims and produced by Imagine Television and Universal Television for NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parenthood_%282010_TV_series%29">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Parenthood (2010 TV series)
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Unlike the preceding series which was produced by MCA/Universal, this film and the following two sequels were produced by New World Television (New World was Marvel's owner at the time) and Bill Bixby's production outfit, which, in association with NBC, took over the
                   <i>
                    Hulk
                   </i>
                   television franchise from former broadcaster CBS.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Incredible_Hulk_Returns">
                    from
                    <span>

                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Code of Vengeance
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is the umbrella title for a series of American television programs, produced by Universal Television, that aired on NBC in 1985 and 1986.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_of_Vengeance">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Code of Vengeance
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     American Dreams
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   was an American television drama program broadcast on the NBC television network, produced by Once A Frog and Dick Clark Productions in association with Universal Network Television and NBC Studios.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Dreams">
                    from
                    <span>
                     American Dreams
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>

                   In 1978, he then switched to Universal Television for NBC, taking the position of assistant to the senior VP.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_Kerner">

                    <span>
                     Jordan Kerner
                    </span>
                   </a>

                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Throughout the years a number of well-known industry directors and casting directors from Universal Television, Warner Brothers, Columbia Pictures, Lorimar TV, NBC, CBS and ABC have been affiliated with the workshop and continue to make bi-monthly guest appearances on a monthly basis.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Actors_Workshop">
                    from
                    <span>

                    </span>

                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>

            <li class="connection" data-id="2097000" data-original-title="The Blue Network, and its immediate predecessor, the NBC Blue Network, were the on-air names of an American radio" data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="blue-network" id="2097000" title="">
             <a data-topic-id="2097000" href="#!/2097000/blue-network">
              <ol class="post-list">
               <li>
                <div class="connection-counter">
                 29
                </div>
                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="2097000" data-topic-title="Blue Network" id="jTopicImage_30" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/78/NBC_Blue_Network.png/128px-NBC_Blue_Network.png"/>
                 <div class="connection-title-and-excerpt">
                  <span class="connection-title" data-count="29" data-id="2097000" data-url-title="blue-network">
                   Blue Network
                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   The Blue Network, and its immediate predecessor, the NBC Blue Network, were the on-air names of an American radio
                  </span>
                 </div>
                </div>

            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="2097000" data-url-title="blue-network" id="connection-expanded-29">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  29
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-29">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NBC_Blue_Network.png" id="jTopicImage_30_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_30" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="2097000" data-topic-title="Blue Network" id="jTopicImage_30" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/78/NBC_Blue_Network.png/128px-NBC_Blue_Network.png"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-29">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-29" id="connection-excerpt-29">
                   The
                   <b>
                    Blue Network
                   </b>
                   , and its immediate predecessor, the
                   <b>
                    NBC Blue Network
                   </b>
                   , were the on-air names of an American radio production and distribution service from 1927 to 1945. Tracing its formal origins back to 1927 as one of the two radio networks owned by the National Broadcasting Company, the Blue Network was born of a divestiture in 1942, arising from anti-trust litigation, and is the direct predecessor of the American Broadcasting Company.
                  </p>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-29">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-29" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-29, #show-more-connection-article-29" href="#" id="show-less-29">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Blue Network
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  On January 1, 1927, NBC formally divided their respective marketing strategies: the "Red Network" offered commercially sponsored entertainment and music programming; the "Blue Network" mostly carried sustaining  or non-sponsored  broadcasts, especially news and cultural programs.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Tracing its formal origins back to 1927 as one of the two radio networks owned by the National Broadcasting Company, the Blue Network was born of a divestiture in 1942, arising from anti-trust litigation, and is the direct predecessor of the American Broadcasting Company.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Network" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Blue Network
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  The three national radio networks already in operationthe Columbia Broadcasting System and the National Broadcasting Company's NBC Red and NBC Bluewere corporate controlled: programming was produced by the network (or by advertising agencies of program sponsors that purchased airtime on the network) and distributed to affiliates, most of which were independently owned.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutual_Broadcasting_System" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Mutual Broadcasting System
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-29" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-29" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-29">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-29">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   With the listening audience increasing in spring and summer 1928, the show's success prompted the Pepsodent Company to bring it to the NBC Blue Network on August 19, 1929.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amos_%27n%27_Andy">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Amos 'n' Andy
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   However, Westinghouse's history with that set of call letters went back even further, as it was the original owner of WJZ radio, the flagship station of NBC's Blue Network, which would eventually become ABC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WJZ-TV">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WJZ-TV
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   ABC was originally formed in 1943 in the wake of an earlier Supreme Court decree effectively ordering the spinoff of the largely secondary-status
                   <i>
                    Blue Network
                   </i>
                   from its then-parent, NBC; its buyer, industrialist Edward J. Noble, tried valiantly to build ABC into an innovative and competitive broadcaster, but by 1951 was rumored to be on the verge of selling the nearly bankrupt operation to CBS, who apparently wanted ABC's critically important owned-and-operated television stations.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonard_Goldenson">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Leonard Goldenson
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   It was also heard from other Chicago venues: the Terrace Casino (at the Morrison Hotel), the College Inn Porterhouse (at the Sherman House) and "the Tiptop Room of the Warwick Allerton Hotel on Chicago's Magnificent Mile," as well as tour broadcasts from other locations in the U.S. It remained a fixture on the ABC radio network (formerly the NBC Blue Network; it became known as ABC in 1945), maintaining its popularity for years and counting among its fans Supreme Court Associate Justice William O. Douglas.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don_McNeill%27s_Breakfast_Club">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Don McNeill's Breakfast Club
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Starting in the 1930s, WLS had been an affiliate of the Blue Network of the National Broadcasting Company (NBC), and as such aired the popular
                   <i>
                    Fibber McGee and Molly
                   </i>
                   and
                   <i>
                    Lum and Abner
                   </i>
                   comedy programs (both produced at the studios of Chicago's NBC-owned stations, WENR and WMAQ) during their early years.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WLS_%28AM%29">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WLS (AM)
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   For many years, KFI was the Los Angeles area affiliate of the NBC radio network, most particularly the NBC Red Network, as distinguished from the NBC Blue Network of less powerful stations, which became the American Broadcasting Company.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KFI">
                    from
                    <span>
                     KFI
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   McNeill hosted
                   <i>
                    The Breakfast Club
                   </i>
                   , which had been Godfrey's direct competition on the NBC Blue Network (later ABC) since Godfrey's days at WJSV.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Godfrey">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Arthur Godfrey
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   He was a noted war correspondent, first with NBC and then with the Blue Network.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Hicks_%28broadcast_journalist%29">
                    from
                    <span>
                     George Hicks (broadcast journalist)
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   In 1943, it was acquired by the Straus family when Edward J. Noble acquired the Blue Network and its owned-and-operated stations from NBC, including WJZ (now WABC) in New York; the Blue Network would later be renamed the American Broadcasting Company (ABC).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WMCA">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WMCA
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   One of the earliest such programs was
                   <i>
                    The Collier Hour
                   </i>
                   , broadcast on the NBC Blue Network from 1927 to 1932.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthology_series">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Anthology series
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   This paved the way for the station to become a charter affiliate of the National Broadcasting Company (NBC) on November 15, 1926, carrying the WJZ-originated NBC Blue Network beginning on January 1, 1927.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WBZ_%28AM%29">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WBZ (AM)
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Duffy's Tavern
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   was a popular American radio situation comedy which ran for a decade on several networks (CBS, 19411942; NBC-Blue Network, 19421944; NBC, 19441951), concluding with the December 28, 1951 broadcast.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duffy%27s_Tavern">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Duffy's Tavern
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                </ul>
                <a class="show-less-connection-texts less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-texts-29" data-to-show="#show-more-connection-texts-29" href="#">
                 SHOW LESS
                </a>
               </div>

                  </a>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-30">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-30" id="connection-excerpt-30">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Bonanza
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an NBC television western series that ran from September 12, 1959, to January 16, 1973. Lasting 14 seasons and 430 episodes, it ranks as the second longest running western series (behind
                   <i>
                    Gunsmoke
                   </i>
                   ), and within the top 10 longest running, live-action American series. The show continues to air in syndication.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-30 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-30, .show-more-connection-article-30" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-30" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-30-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-30">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Bonanza
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an NBC television western series that ran from September 12, 1959, to January 16, 1973. Lasting 14 seasons and 430 episodes, it ranks as the second longest running western series (behind
                     <i>
                      Gunsmoke
                     </i>
                     ), and within the top 10 longest running, live-action American series. The show continues to air in syndication.
                     <br/>
                     The show is set around the 1860s and it centers on the Cartwright family, who live in the area of Virginia City, Nevada, bordering Lake Tahoe. The series stars Lorne Greene, Dan Blocker, Michael Landon, Pernell Roberts (who left after six seasons), and later David Canary and Mitch Vogel.
                     <br/>
                     The title "Bonanza" is a term used by miners in regard to a large vein or deposit of ore, and commonly refers to the Comstock Lode.
                     <br/>
                     In 2002,
                     <i>
                      Bonanza
                     </i>
                     was ranked No. 43 on TV Guide's 50 Greatest TV Shows of All Time, and in 2013
                     <i>
                      TV Guide
                     </i>
                     included it in its list of The 60 Greatest Dramas of All Time. The time period for the television series is roughly between 1861 (Season 1) to 1867 (Season 13) during and shortly after the American Civil War.
                     <br/>
                     During the summer of 1972, NBC aired reruns of episodes from the 19671970 period in prime time on Tuesday evening under the title
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Ponderosa
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     .
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-30" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-30, #show-more-connection-article-30" href="#" id="show-less-30">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-31">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-31" id="connection-excerpt-31">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Wagon Train
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American Western series that ran on NBC 195762 and then on ABC 196265, although the network also aired daytime repeats, as
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Major Adams, Trailmaster
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   and
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Trailmaster
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   (post-1961 episodes without original series lead Ward Bond), from January 1963 to September 1965. The show debuted at #15 in the Nielsen ratings, rose to
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-31 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-31, .show-more-connection-article-31" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-31" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-31-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-31">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Wagon Train
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American Western series that ran on NBC 195762 and then on ABC 196265, although the network also aired daytime repeats, as
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Major Adams, Trailmaster
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     and
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Trailmaster
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     (post-1961 episodes without original series lead Ward Bond), from January 1963 to September 1965. The show debuted at #15 in the Nielsen ratings, rose to #2 in the next three seasons, and peaked at #1 in the 196162 television season. After moving to ABC in the autumn of 1962, the ratings began to decline, and
                     <i>
                      Wagon Train
                     </i>
                     did not again make the Top 20 listing.
                     <br/>
                     The series initially starred veteran movie supporting actor Ward Bond as the wagon master, later replaced upon his death by John McIntire, and Robert Horton as the scout, subsequently replaced by lookalike Robert Fuller a year after Horton had decided to leave the series.
                     <br/>
                     The series was inspired by the 1950 film
                     <i>
                      Wagon Master
                     </i>
                     directed by John Ford and starring Ben Johnson, Harry Carey Jr. and Ward Bond, and harkens back to the early widescreen wagon train epic
                     <i>
                      The Big Trail
                     </i>
                     (1930) starring John Wayne and featuring Bond in his first major screen appearance playing a supporting role. Horton's buckskin outfit as the scout in the first season of the television series resembles Wayne's, who also played the wagon train's scout in the earlier film.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-31" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-31, #show-more-connection-article-31" href="#" id="show-less-31">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-32">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-32" id="connection-excerpt-32">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Heroes
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American science fiction television drama series created by Tim Kring that appeared on NBC for four seasons from September 25, 2006 through February 8, 2010. The series tells the stories of ordinary people who discover superhuman abilities, and how these abilities take effect in the characters' lives. The series emulates the aesthetic
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-32 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-32, .show-more-connection-article-32" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-32" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-32-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-32">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Heroes
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American science fiction television drama series created by Tim Kring that appeared on NBC for four seasons from September 25, 2006 through February 8, 2010. The series tells the stories of ordinary people who discover superhuman abilities, and how these abilities take effect in the characters' lives. The series emulates the aesthetic style and storytelling of American comic books, using multi-episode story arcs that build upon a larger, more encompassing narrative. The series was produced by Tailwind Productions in association with Universal Media Studios. It was filmed primarily in Los Angeles, California.
                     <br/>
                     Four complete seasons aired, ending on February 8, 2010. The critically acclaimed first season had a run of 23 episodes and garnered an average of 14.3 million viewers in the United States, receiving the highest rating for an NBC drama premiere in five years. The second season of
                     <i>
                      Heroes
                     </i>
                     attracted an average of 13.1 million viewers in the U.S., and marked NBC's sole series among the top 20 ranked programs in total viewership for the 20072008 season.
                     <i>
                      Heroes
                     </i>
                     has earned a number of awards and nominations, including Primetime Emmy Awards, Golden Globes, People's Choice Awards, and British Academy Television Awards.
                     <br/>
                     An online extension of the series,
                     <i>
                      Heroes 360 Experience
                     </i>
                     , later rebranded as
                     <i>
                      Heroes Evolutions
                     </i>
                     , was created to explore the
                     <i>
                      Heroes
                     </i>
                     universe and provides insight into the show's mythology. Other official
                     <i>
                      Heroes
                     </i>
                     media include magazines, action figures, tie-in and interactive websites, a mobile game, a novel, clothing and other merchandise. In the fall of 2008, NBC Digital Entertainment released a series of online content for the summer, including more original web content, wireless iTV interactivity, graphic novels available for mobile viewing and webisodes.
                     <br/>
                     A 13-episode miniseries entitled
                     <i>
                      Heroes Reborn
                     </i>
                     will premiere on NBC on September 24, 2015. Additionally, comic book writer Cullen Bunn will be writing an ongoing comic book continuing
                     <i>
                      Heroes
                     </i>
                     , called
                     <i>
                      Heroes: Season Five
                     </i>
                     ; a release date and artist has yet to be determined.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-32" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-32, #show-more-connection-article-32" href="#" id="show-less-32">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-33">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-33" id="connection-excerpt-33">
                   The
                   <b>
                    Cable News Network
                   </b>
                   (
                   <b>
                    CNN
                   </b>
                   ) is an American basic cable and satellite television channel that is owned by the Turner Broadcasting System division of Time Warner. The 24-hour cable news channel was founded in 1980 by American media proprietor Ted Turner. Upon its launch, CNN was the first television channel to provide 24-hour news coverage, and was the first all-news television channel in the United States.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-33 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-33, .show-more-connection-article-33" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-33" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-33-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-33">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     The
                     <b>
                      Cable News Network
                     </b>
                     (
                     <b>
                      CNN
                     </b>
                     ) is an American basic cable and satellite television channel that is owned by the Turner Broadcasting System division of Time Warner. The 24-hour cable news channel was founded in 1980 by American media proprietor Ted Turner. Upon its launch, CNN was the first television channel to provide 24-hour news coverage, and was the first all-news television channel in the United States.
                     <br/>
                     While the news channel has numerous affiliates, CNN primarily broadcasts from the Time Warner Center in New York City, and studios in Washington, D.C. and Los Angeles, its headquarters at the CNN Center in Atlanta is only used for weekend programming. CNN is sometimes referred to as
                     <b>
                      CNN/U.S.
                     </b>
                     to distinguish the American channel from its international sister network, CNN International. As of August 2010, CNN is available in over 100 million U.S. households. Broadcast coverage of the U.S. channel extends to over 890,000 American hotel rooms, as well as carriage on cable and satellite providers throughout Canada. Globally, CNN programming airs through CNN International, which can be seen by viewers in over 212 countries and territories.
                     <br/>
                     As of February 2015, CNN is available to approximately 96,289,000 cable, satellite and, telco television households (82.7% of households with at least one television set) in the United States.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-33" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-33, #show-more-connection-article-33" href="#" id="show-less-33">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-33 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-33" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-33" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-33-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                   <b>
                    NBC News
                   </b>
                   is a division of the American broadcast network NBC. The division operates under NBCUniversal News Group, a subsidiary of NBCUniversal. The group's various operations report to the president of NBC News, Deborah Turness.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-34 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-34, .show-more-connection-article-34" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-34" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-34-short">
                   <span>

                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-34">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      NBC News
                     </b>
                     is a division of the American broadcast network NBC. The division operates under NBCUniversal News Group, a subsidiary of NBCUniversal. The group's various operations report to the president of NBC News, Deborah Turness.
                     <br/>
                     NBC News aired the first news program in American broadcast television history on February 21, 1940. The group's broadcasts are produced and aired from the GE Building in Rockefeller Center, NBC's headquarters in New York.
                     <br/>
                     The division presides over America's number-one-rated newscast,
                     <i>
                      NBC Nightly News
                     </i>
                     , and the longest-running television series in American history,
                     <i>
                      Meet the Press with Chuck Todd
                     </i>
                     . NBC News also offers 70 years of rare historic footage from the NBCUniversal Archives online.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-34" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-34, #show-more-connection-article-34" href="#" id="show-less-34">
