            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="10839777" data-url-title="telemundo" id="connection-expanded-35">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  35
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-35">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_36_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_36" data-searched="" data-topic-id="10839777" data-topic-title="Telemundo" id="jTopicImage_36" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-35">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-35" id="connection-excerpt-35">
                   <b>
                    Telemundo
                   </b>
                   (
                   <small>
                    Spanish pronunciation:
                   </small>
                   <span>
                    [telemundo]
                   </span>
                   ) is an American Spanish language broadcast television network that is owned by the NBCUniversal Television Group division of NBCUniversal. The network broadcasts programs, including several produced by the network itself, aimed at Hispanic and Latino Americans in the U.S., and audiences around the world  featuring a mix of telenovelas, sports,
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-35 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-35, .show-more-connection-article-35" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-35" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-35-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-35">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Telemundo
                     </b>
                     (
                     <small>
                      Spanish pronunciation:
                     </small>
                     <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
                      [telemundo]
                     </span>
                     ) is an American Spanish language broadcast television network that is owned by the NBCUniversal Television Group division of NBCUniversal. The network broadcasts programs, including several produced by the network itself, aimed at Hispanic and Latino Americans in the U.S., and audiences around the world  featuring a mix of telenovelas, sports, reality television series, news programming, and feature films (both Spanish-dubbed versions of American films and imported films produced in Spanish-speaking countries)
                     <br/>
                     In addition to the broadcast network, Telemundo also operates NBC Universo, a cable and satellite channel specializing in programming geared towards a young Hispanic audience; Telemundo Digital Media, which distributes original programming content across digital and mobile networks, and the telemundo.com and mun2.tv websites; Puerto Rico television station WKAQ-TV, whose signal reaches 99% of all television households in the U.S. territory; and international distribution arm Telemundo Internacional. Telemundo is the second-largest provider of Spanish-language content worldwide behind American competitor Univision, with its programming syndicated worldwide to more than 100 countries in over 35 languages.
                     <br/>
                     Telemundo is headquartered in the Miami suburb of Hialeah, Florida, and has 1,900 employees worldwide. The majority of Telemundo shows and programs are filmed at a studio facility operated by the network in Miami. In 2011, 85% of Telemundo's telenovelas were filmed in Miami. The average hour-long primetime drama costs the network $70,000 to produce.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-35" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-35, #show-more-connection-article-35" href="#" id="show-less-35">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-35 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-35" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-35" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-35-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Telemundo
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  In October 2001, NBC acquired Spanish-language network Telemundo from Liberty Media and Sony Pictures Entertainment for $2.7 billion, beating out other bidders including CBS/Viacom.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  On April 12, 2002, Telemundo was purchased by NBC (which itself was merged with Vivendi Universal the following year to become the present-day NBCUniversal) for $2.7 billion.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telemundo" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Telemundo
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  The FCC reserved final say on which stations would be allowed to transition on February 17 and which ones would be required to continue analog broadcasts, depending on how many viewers in each market have been determined not ready for the transition Owned &amp; Operated stations of five major networks (ABC, CBS, Fox, NBC and Telemundo, plus the CW, myNetworkTV and independent stations owned by CBS and myNetworkTV stations owned by Fox), as well as the station groups of Gannett, Hearst-Argyle and Meredith, committed to keeping all or most of their analog signals active until the new June 12 cutoff date.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_television_transition_in_the_United_States" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Digital television transition in the United States
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-35" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-35" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-35">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-35">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   On the other hand, several other television stations in the same market  WABC-TV (ABC), WCBS-TV (CBS), WNBC (NBC), WNJU (Telemundo), WNYW (Fox), WWOR-TV (MyNetworkTV), WPXN-TV (Ion Television), WXTV-DT (Univision) and WFUT-DT (UniMs)  are O&amp;Os.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Network_affiliate">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Network affiliate
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Comcast operates multiple cable-only channels (including E! Entertainment Television, the Golf Channel, and NBCSN), over-the-air national broadcast network channels (NBC and Telemundo), the film production studio Universal Pictures, and Universal Parks &amp; Resorts, with a global total of nearly 200 family entertainment locations and attractions in the U.S. and several other countries including U.A.E., South Korea, Russia and China, with several new locations reportedly planned and being developed for future operation.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comcast">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Comcast
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Lpez noted that the Fox Broadcasting Company saw "similar dynamics in play" when it launched in October 1986 against established English language networks ABC, NBC and CBS; MundoFox, he added, would seek to replicate Fox's early years while launching against established Spanish language networks Univision, Telemundo and Azteca Amrica.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MundoFox">
                    from
                    <span>
                     MundoFox
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   DirecTV also offers local channels like CBS, ABC, NBC, Fox, PBS, The CW, Telemundo, Azteca, Univision, ION Television (in markets that carry that network), and some independent stations in markets covering over 99.2% of U.S. TV households.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DirecTV">
                    from
                    <span>

                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Jeopardy!
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American television game show created by Merv Griffin. The show features a quiz competition in which contestants are presented with general knowledge clues in the form of answers, and must phrase their responses in the form of questions. The original daytime version debuted on NBC on March 30, 1964, and aired until
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-36 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-36, .show-more-connection-article-36" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-36" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-36-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-36">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Jeopardy!
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American television game show created by Merv Griffin. The show features a quiz competition in which contestants are presented with general knowledge clues in the form of answers, and must phrase their responses in the form of questions. The original daytime version debuted on NBC on March 30, 1964, and aired until January 3, 1975. A weekly nighttime syndicated edition aired from September 1974 to September 1975, and a revival,
                     <i>
                      The All-New Jeopardy!
                     </i>
                     , ran on NBC from October 1978 to March 1979. A daily syndicated version premiered on September 10, 1984, and is still airing, making it by far the program's most successful incarnation.
                     <br/>
                     Both NBC versions and the weekly syndicated version were hosted by Art Fleming. Don Pardo served as announcer until 1975, and John Harlan announced for the 197879 show. Since its inception, the daily syndicated version has featured Alex Trebek as host and Johnny Gilbert as announcer.
                     <br/>
                     With 7,000 episodes aired, the daily syndicated version of
                     <i>
                      Jeopardy!
                     </i>
                     has won a record 31 Daytime Emmy Awards and is the only game show to be honored with the Peabody Award. In 2013, the program was ranked No. 45 on
                     <i>
                      TV Guide
                     </i>
                     's list of the 60 greatest shows in American television history.
                     <i>
                      Jeopardy!
                     </i>
                     has also gained a worldwide following with regional adaptations in many other countries. The daily syndicated series' 31st season premiered on September 15, 2014.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-36" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-36, #show-more-connection-article-36" href="#" id="show-less-36">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>

                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-37">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_38_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_38" data-searched="" data-topic-id="3613092" data-topic-title="NBC Sunday Night Football" id="jTopicImage_38" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-37">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-37" id="connection-excerpt-37">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     NBC Sunday Night Football
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is a weekly television broadcast of National Football League (NFL) games on NBC in the United States. It began airing on August 6, 2006 with the Pro Football Hall of Fame Game, which opened that year's preseason. NBC took over the rights to the Sunday prime time game telecasts from ESPN,
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-37 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-37, .show-more-connection-article-37" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-37" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-37-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-37">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       NBC Sunday Night Football
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is a weekly television broadcast of National Football League (NFL) games on NBC in the United States. It began airing on August 6, 2006 with the Pro Football Hall of Fame Game, which opened that year's preseason. NBC took over the rights to the Sunday prime time game telecasts from ESPN, which carried the broadcasts from 1987 to 2005 (concurrently with NBC assuming the rights to Sunday evening regular-season games, ESPN took over the broadcast rights to
                     <i>
                      Monday Night Football
                     </i>
                     from sister network ABC beginning with the 2006 season).
                     <br/>
                     For the 201112 season, Nielsen ranked NBC's
                     <i>
                      Sunday Night Football
                     </i>
                     as the most-watched program on U.S. network television, beating
                     <i>
                      American Idol
                     </i>
                     , which held that honor for eight consecutive seasons beginning in 2004;
                     <i>
                      Sunday Night Football
                     </i>
                     repeated this feat as the most-watched program for the 201314 season.
                     <br/>
                     As of 2014, Al Michaels serves as the play-by-play announcer for the broadcasts, with Cris Collinsworth as the color commentator and Michele Tafoya as the sideline reporter. Upon NBC's assumption of the Sunday prime time game rights, Fred Gaudelli and Drew Esocoff, who serve as the respective lead producer and director, joined
                     <i>
                      Sunday Night Football
                     </i>
                     in the same positions they held during the latter portion of the ABC era of
                     <i>
                      Monday Night Football
                     </i>
                     . John Madden, the color commentator for the first three years of the program, retired prior to the 2009 season; he was succeeded in that role by Collinsworth.
                     <br/>
                     Since 2014, sister cable channel NBC Universo has carried Spanish-language audio simulcasts of select games, after years of aborted attempts to simulcast the games on Telemundo; as with the NFL's other television partners, NBC provides Spanish-language audio feed of the game broadcasts via second audio program (SAP), although the network promotes the simulcasts as being "provided by Telemundo". With the former mun2's relaunch on February 1, 2015, NBC Universo simulcast Super Bowl XLIX with NBC, with the channel expected to carry Spanish-language simulcasts of NFL games and NBC Sports properties.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-37" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-37, #show-more-connection-article-37" href="#" id="show-less-37">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-37 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-37" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-37" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-37-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

                  <i>

                  <i>

                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:New_York_New_Amsterdam_Theatre_2003.jpg" id="jTopicImage_39_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_39" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="725252" data-topic-title="Broadway theatre" id="jTopicImage_39" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/New_York_New_Amsterdam_Theatre_2003.jpg/128px-New_York_New_Amsterdam_Theatre_2003.jpg"/>
                   <span class="copyright">

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-38">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-38" id="connection-excerpt-38">
                   <span>
                   </span>
                   <br/>
                   <b>
                    Broadway theatre
                   </b>
                   , commonly known as
                   <b>
                    Broadway
                   </b>
                   , refers to the theatrical performances presented in the 40 professional theatres with 500 or more seats located in the Theater District and Lincoln Center along Broadway, in the New York City borough of Manhattan. Along with London's West End theatres, Broadway theatres are widely considered to represent the most commercially successful level of commercial theatre in the English-speaking world.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-38 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-38, .show-more-connection-article-38" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-38" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-38-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-38">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <span>
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      Broadway theatre
                     </b>
                     , commonly known as
                     <b>
                      Broadway
                     </b>
                     , refers to the theatrical performances presented in the 40 professional theatres with 500 or more seats located in the Theater District and Lincoln Center along Broadway, in the New York City borough of Manhattan. Along with London's West End theatres, Broadway theatres are widely considered to represent the most commercially successful level of commercial theatre in the English-speaking world.
                     <br/>
                     The Broadway Theater District is a popular tourist attraction in New York City. According to The Broadway League, Broadway shows sold a record US$1.36 billion worth of tickets in 2014, an increase of 14% over the previous year. Attendance in 2014 stood at 13.13 million, a 13% increase over 2013.
                     <br/>
                     The great majority of Broadway shows are musicals. Historian Martin Shefter argues, "'Broadway musicals,' culminating in the productions of Richard Rodgers and Oscar Hammerstein, became enormously influential forms of American popular culture" and helped make New York City the cultural capital of the nation.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-38" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-38, #show-more-connection-article-38" href="#" id="show-less-38">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-38 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-38" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-38" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-38-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Broadway theatre
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  In 1955, NBC broadcast a live production in color of
                  <i>
                   Peter Pan
                  </i>
                  , a new Broadway musical adaptation of J. M. Barrie's beloved play, on the
                  <i>
                   Producers' Showcase
                  </i>
                  anthology series, The first such telecast of its kind, the broadcast starred the musical's entire original cast, led by Mary Martin as Peter and Cyril Ritchard in a dual role as Mr. Darling and Captain Hook.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Containing primarily Broadway showtunes, the special was taped before a live studio audience in mid-1969 and originally broadcast November 12, 1969 on NBC.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G.I.T._on_Broadway" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    G.I.T. on Broadway
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  He went on to play piano for the Schwartz Broadway show
                  <i>
                   The Magic Show
                  </i>
                  in 1974, then became a member of the house band on NBC's popular
                  <i>
                   Saturday Night Live
                  </i>
                  (
                  <i>
                   SNL
                  </i>
                  ) television program from 1975 to 1980 (except for a brief departure in 1977).
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Shaffer" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Paul Shaffer
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-38" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-38" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-38">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-38">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Other residents of note include: songwriter Frank Loesser, who wrote for Broadway shows including
                   <i>
                    Guys and Dolls
                   </i>
                   ; the playwright, Guy Bolton, who collaborated with Wodehouse on
                   <i>
                    Anything Goes;
                   </i>
                   and Dave Garroway, the original host of NBC's
                   <i>
                    Today Show
                   </i>
                   when it first aired in January, 1952.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remsenburg%2C_New_York">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Remsenburg, New York
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   He also possessed a deep background in theatrical and radio entertainment, having worked as a lawyer for brothers Lee and Jacob J. Shubert, the founders of Manhattan's Broadway district, and as a producer for the popular radio shows
                   <i>
                    The Life of Riley
                   </i>
                   on CBS and
                   <i>
                    Time to Smile
                   </i>
                   starring Eddie Cantor on NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WKSS">
                    from
                    <span>
                     WKSS
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   He wrote the score for the Broadway play
                   <i>
                    The Flowering Peach
                   </i>
                   by Clifford Odets in 1954, a ballet for Martha Graham (
                   <i>
                    Ardent Song
                   </i>
                   , also in 1954), and two scores for NBC documentaries on India and Southeast Asia (1955 and 1957).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Hovhaness">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Alan Hovhaness
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                </ul>

            <li class="connection" data-id="496028" data-original-title="The Eastern Time Zone (ET) is a time zone encompassing 17 U.S. states in the eastern part of the contiguous United" data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="eastern-time-zone" id="496028" title="">

            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="496028" data-url-title="eastern-time-zone" id="connection-expanded-39">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  39
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-39">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Timezoneswest.PNG" id="jTopicImage_40_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_40" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="496028" data-topic-title="Eastern Time Zone" id="jTopicImage_40" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Timezoneswest.PNG/128px-Timezoneswest.PNG"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-39">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-39" id="connection-excerpt-39">
                   The
                   <b>
                    Eastern Time Zone
                   </b>
                   (
                   <b>
                    ET
                   </b>
                   ) is a time zone encompassing 17 U.S. states in the eastern part of the contiguous United States, parts of eastern Canada, the state of Quintana Roo in Mexico, Panama in Central America and the Caribbean Islands.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-39 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-39, .show-more-connection-article-39" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-39" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-39-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-39">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     The
                     <b>
                      Eastern Time Zone
                     </b>
                     (
                     <b>
                      ET
                     </b>
                     ) is a time zone encompassing 17 U.S. states in the eastern part of the contiguous United States, parts of eastern Canada, the state of Quintana Roo in Mexico, Panama in Central America and the Caribbean Islands.
                     <br/>
                     Places that use
                     <b>
                      Eastern Standard Time
                     </b>
                     (
                     <b>
                      EST
                     </b>
                     ) when observing standard time (autumn/winter) are 5 hours behind Coordinated Universal Time (UTC05:00).
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      Eastern Daylight Time
                     </b>
                     (
                     <b>
                      EDT
                     </b>
                     ), when observing daylight saving time (spring/summer) is 4 hours behind Coordinated Universal Time (UTC04:00).
                     <br/>
                     In the northern parts of the time zone, during the second Sunday in March, at 2:00a.m. EST, clocks are advanced to 3:00a.m. EDT leaving a one-hour "gap". During the first Sunday in November, at 2:00a.m. EDT, clocks are moved back to 1:00a.m. EST, thus "duplicating" one hour. Southern parts of the zone (Panama and the Caribbean) do not observe daylight saving time.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-39" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-39, #show-more-connection-article-39" href="#" id="show-less-39">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-39 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-39" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-39" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-39-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Eastern Time Zone
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  The package was aimed at attracting viewers to NBC stations in the half-hour preceding prime time (8:00p.m. in the Eastern and Pacific Time Zone, 7:00p.m. elsewhere), and was conceived as a result of the FCC's loosening of the Prime Time Access Rule, legislation passed in 1971 that required networks to turn over the 7:30p.m. (Eastern) time slot to local stations to program local or syndicated content; and the relaxation of the Financial Interest and Syndication Rules, which had prevented networks from producing content from their own syndication units to fill the void.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  National broadcast networks (ABC, CBS, The CW, Fox Network, NBC) generally have two primary feeds, an eastern feed for Eastern and Central time zones, and a tape-delayed western feed for the Pacific Time Zone.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Eastern Time Zone
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  One week before the 2008 general election, Obama purchased a 30-minute slot at 8 p.m. Eastern and Pacific Time during primetime on seven major networks (NBC, CBS, MSNBC, Fox, BET, TV One and Univision (with Spanish subtitles)) to present a "closing argument" to his campaign.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infomercial" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Infomercial
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-39" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-39" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-39">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-39">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   It came to be known as the
                   <i>
                    Heidi
                   </i>
                   Game because the NBC Television Network controversially broke away from the game, with the Jets still winning, to air the television film
                   <i>
                    Heidi
                   </i>
                   at 7 p.m. in the Eastern Time Zone.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heidi_Game">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Heidi Game
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   During the 1988 Writers Guild of America strike, networks benefited from sports programming, including NBC, which relied on the Summer Olympics in September and the World Series in October, and ABC, which in addition to its postseason baseball coverage, moved up the start time for the early weeks of
                   <i>
                    Monday Night Football
                   </i>
                   (when Al Michaels was unavailable to do play-by-play on
                   <i>
                    Monday Night Football
                   </i>
                   , which he had done for ABC beginning in 1986 due to his postseason baseball duties, Frank Gifford covered for him) from 9 p.m. ET to 8 p.m. ET (
                   <i>
                    MacGyver
                   </i>
                   , which normally aired at 8 p.m., was not yet ready with new episodes).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_ABC">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Major League Baseball on ABC
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Due to the show's success, over the summer of 1990 the Fox Network decided to switch
                   <i>
                    The Simpsons
                   </i>
                   time slot so that it would move from 8:00p.m. ET on Sunday night to the same time on Thursday, where it would compete with
                   <i>
                    The Cosby Show
                   </i>
                   on NBC, the number one show at the time.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Simpsons">
                    from
                    <span>
                     The Simpsons
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Late-night local newscasts are traditionally broadcast at 11:00 p.m. local time on owned-and-operated stations and affiliates of the Big Three television networks (CBS, NBC and ABC) and the major Spanish language networks (Univision and Telemundo) in the United States, and of CTV, Global and in a few markets, CBC Television, in Canada that are located in the Eastern and Pacific Time Zones.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late-night_news">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Late-night news
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   This episode originally aired on May 7, 1987, on NBC at 9:00pm (Eastern) / 8:00pm (Central) and scored a 28.4 rating and 45 share, was watched by 24.8 million homes, and ranked #1 in Nielsen ratings.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I_Do%2C_Adieu">
                    from
                    <span>
                     I Do, Adieu
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   It originally aired on May 7, 1987 on NBC at 9:00pm (Eastern) / 8:00pm (Central).
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I_Do%2C_Adieu">
                    from
                    <span>
                     I Do, Adieu

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-40">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-40" id="connection-excerpt-40">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     NBC Nightly News
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   (titled since June 22, 2015 as
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     NBC Nightly News with Lester Holt
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   for its weeknight broadcasts) is the flagship daily evening television news program of NBC News, the news division of the NBC television network in the United States. First aired on August 3, 1970, the program is currently the most watched
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-40 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-40, .show-more-connection-article-40" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-40" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-40-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-40">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       NBC Nightly News
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     (titled since June 22, 2015 as
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       NBC Nightly News with Lester Holt
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     for its weeknight broadcasts) is the flagship daily evening television news program of NBC News, the news division of the NBC television network in the United States. First aired on August 3, 1970, the program is currently the most watched network newscast in the United States, with an average of 9.3 million viewers, just a few thousand more than its nearest rival, ABC's
                     <i>
                      World News Tonight
                     </i>
                     .
                     <i>
                      NBC Nightly News
                     </i>
                     is produced from Studio 3B at NBC Studios at 30 Rockefeller Center in New York City.
                     <br/>
                     Since 2015, the weeknight broadcasts have been anchored by Lester Holt and the weekend editions have been anchored by various people. Previous anchors have included David Brinkley, John Chancellor, Tom Brokaw and Brian Williams.
                     <br/>
                     The program is broadcast live over most NBC stations from 6:30 to 7:00p.m. Eastern Time seven days a week; a special "Western Edition" of the program occasionally features updated information on news stories covered during the original telecast for Pacific Time Zone viewers. Its current theme music, "The Mission," which debuted in 1985, was composed by John Williams.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-40" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-40, #show-more-connection-article-40" href="#" id="show-less-40">

                <li>

                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-41">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_42_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_42" data-searched="" data-topic-id="173629" data-topic-title="Law &amp; Order" id="jTopicImage_42" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-41">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-41" id="connection-excerpt-41">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Law &amp; Order
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American police procedural and legal drama television series, created by Dick Wolf and part of the
                   <i>
                    Law &amp; Order
                   </i>
                   franchise. It originally aired on NBC and, in syndication, on various cable networks.
                   <i>
                    Law &amp; Order
                   </i>
                   premiered on September 13, 1990, and completed its 20th and final season on May 24,
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-41 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-41, .show-more-connection-article-41" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-41" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-41-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-41">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Law &amp; Order
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American police procedural and legal drama television series, created by Dick Wolf and part of the
                     <i>
                      Law &amp; Order
                     </i>
                     franchise. It originally aired on NBC and, in syndication, on various cable networks.
                     <i>
                      Law &amp; Order
                     </i>
                     premiered on September 13, 1990, and completed its 20th and final season on May 24, 2010. At the time of its cancellation,
                     <i>
                      Law &amp; Order
                     </i>
                     was the longest-running crime drama on American primetime television. Its record of 20 seasons is a tie with
                     <i>
                      Gunsmoke
                     </i>
                     for the longest-running live-action scripted American prime-time series with ongoing characters, although it had fewer episodes than
                     <i>
                      Gunsmoke
                     </i>
                     , and both series are surpassed by the animated series
                     <i>
                      The Simpsons
                     </i>
                     (in its 25th season as of 2013).
                     <br/>
                     Set and filmed in New York City, the series follows a two-part approach: The first half hour is the investigation of a crime (usually murder) and apprehension of a suspect by New York City Police Department homicide detectives; the second half is the prosecution of the defendant by the New York County Manhattan District Attorney's Office. Plots are often based on real cases that recently made headlines, although the motivation for the crime and the perpetrator may be different.
                     <br/>
                     The show has been noted for its revolving cast over the years. Season 1 starred George Dzundza as Sergeant Max Greevey, Chris Noth as Detective Mike Logan, Dann Florek as Captain Donald Cragen, Michael Moriarty as Executive Assistant District Attorney Ben Stone, Richard Brooks as Assistant District Attorney Paul Robinette and Steven Hill as District Attorney Adam Schiff. After numerous cast shuffles, its final season starred Jeremy Sisto as Detective Cyrus Lupo, Anthony Anderson as Detective Kevin Bernard, S. Epatha Merkerson as Lieutenant Anita Van Buren, Linus Roache as Executive Assistant District Attorney Michael Cutter, Alana de la Garza as Assistant District Attorney Connie Rubirosa, and Sam Waterston as District Attorney Jack McCoy. Another one of the series' most notable performers was Jerry Orbach as Detective Lennie Briscoe, who starred on the show for twelve years (seasons 314).
                     <br/>
                     The success of the series has led to the creation of additional shows, making
                     <i>
                      Law &amp; Order
                     </i>
                     a franchise, with also a television film, several video games, and international adaptations of the series. It has won and has been nominated for numerous awards over the years, including a number of Emmy Awards. On May 14, 2010, NBC announced that it had cancelled
                     <i>
                      Law &amp; Order
                     </i>
                     and would air the final episode on May 24, 2010. Immediately following the show's cancellation, Wolf stated that he was attempting to find a new home for the series and would also consider a "last resort" plan to conclude the show with a two-hour TV film to air on NBC. In July 2010, however, he indicated that those attempts had failed and declared that the series had now "moved to the history books".
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-41" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-41, #show-more-connection-article-41" href="#" id="show-less-41">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-41 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-41" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-41" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-41-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- /Connection Article -->
              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Law &amp; Order
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  On May 14, 2010, NBC officially canceled the show, opting instead to pick up
                  <i>
                   Law &amp; Order: Los Angeles
                  </i>
                  for a first season, and renewed
                  <i>
                  </i>
                  for a twelfth.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_%26_Order" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Law &amp; Order
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  <i>
                   Law &amp; Order
                  </i>
                  premiered September 13, 1990, and aired on NBC, with 456 episodes having been produced.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_%26_Order" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Law &amp; Order
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  NBC had been pushing for the producers to add female characters to the all male cast.

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-42">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-42" id="connection-excerpt-42">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     The Tonight Show
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American late-night talk show broadcast from the Rockefeller Center in New York City and airing on NBC since 1954. It is the world's longest-running talk show, and the longest running, regularly scheduled entertainment program in the United States. It is the third-longest-running show on NBC, after only the news and talk shows
                   <i>
                    Today
                   </i>
                   and
                   <i>
                    Meet the Press
                   </i>
                   .
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-42 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-42, .show-more-connection-article-42" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-42" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-42-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-42">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       The Tonight Show
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American late-night talk show broadcast from the Rockefeller Center in New York City and airing on NBC since 1954. It is the world's longest-running talk show, and the longest running, regularly scheduled entertainment program in the United States. It is the third-longest-running show on NBC, after only the news and talk shows
                     <i>
                      Today
                     </i>
                     and
                     <i>
                      Meet the Press
                     </i>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     Over the course of more than sixty years,
                     <i>
                      The Tonight Show
                     </i>
                     has undergone only minor title changes. It aired under the name
                     <i>
                      Tonight
                     </i>
                     for several of its early years, eventually settling on
                     <i>
                      The Tonight Show
                     </i>
                     after the seating of long-time host Johnny Carson in 1962. In later decades, network programmers, advertisers, and the show's announcers would refer to the show by including the name of the host; for example, it is currently announced as
                     <i>
                      The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon
                     </i>
                     . In 1957, the show briefly tried a more news-style format. It has otherwise remained a talk show throughout its run.
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      The Tonight Show
                     </i>
                     began broadcasting in 1954. It has had six official hosts, beginning with Steve Allen (195457), followed by Jack Paar (195762), Johnny Carson (196292), Jay Leno (19922009, 201014), Conan O'Brien (200910), and Jimmy Fallon (2014present). It has had several recurring guest hosts, a practice especially common during the Paar and Carson eras.
                     <br/>
                     Johnny Carson is the longest-serving host to date.
                     <i>
                      The Tonight Show Starring Johnny Carson
                     </i>
                     aired for 30 seasons between October 1962 and May 1992. Leno, however, has the record of having hosted the greatest number of total televised episodes. Leno's record is the result of his two separate tenures.
                     <br/>
                     Outside of its brief run as a news show in 1957, Conan O'Brien is the shortest-serving host. O'Brien hosted 146 episodes over the course of less than eight months. Current host Jimmy Fallon took the helm on February 17, 2014. Fallon had previously hosted
                     <i>
                      Late Night
                     </i>
                     , and before
                     <i>
                      Late Night
                     </i>
                     he was a popular member of the cast on
                     <i>
                      Saturday Night Live
                     </i>
                     .
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-42" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-42, #show-more-connection-article-42" href="#" id="show-less-42">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-42 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-42" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-42" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-42-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

              <div class="frame">
               <!-- Connection Texts -->
               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                The Tonight Show
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  NBC's last major radio programming push, beginning on June 12, 1955, was
                  <i>
                   Monitor
                  </i>
                  , a creation of NBC President Sylvester "Pat" Weaver, who also created the innovative programs
                  <i>
                   Today
                  </i>
                  ,
                  <i>
                   The Tonight Show
                  </i>
                  and
                  <i>
                   Home
                  </i>
                  for the companion television network.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  In July 1957, NBC returned the program to a talk/variety show format once again, with Jack Paar becoming the new solo host of the show.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Tonight_Show" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  and began its historic run on the full NBC network.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Tonight_Show" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-42" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-42" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-42">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-42">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The following year, on September 27, 1954, the show went on the full NBC network as
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   , with fellow radio personality Gene Rayburn (who later went on to host hit game shows such as
                   <i>
                    Match Game
                   </i>
                   , 19621982) as the original announcer.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Allen">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Steve Allen
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The first version of
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   ,
                   <i>
                    Tonight Starring Steve Allen
                   </i>
                   , debuted in 1954 on NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late-night_talk_show">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Late-night talk show
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     The Tonight Show with Conan O'Brien
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American late-night talk show that featured Conan O'Brien as host from June 1, 2009 to January 22, 2010 as part of NBC's long-running
                   <i>
                    Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   franchise.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Conan_O%27Brien">
                    from
                    <span>
                     The Tonight Show with Conan O'Brien
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   A sequel to
                   <i>
                    The Late Shift
                   </i>
                   called
                   <i>
                    The War for Late Night
                   </i>
                   , based on the controversy involving Jay Leno, Conan O'Brien,
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   and NBC was released on November 4, 2010.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Late_Shift_%28book%29">
                    from
                    <span>
                     The Late Shift (book)
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   In the summer of 1993, David Letterman, who had spent over 13 years at NBC and the previous 11 as the host of the popular post-
                   <i>
                    Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   program
                   <i>
                    Late Night
                   </i>
                   , left the network due to his dissatisfaction with being passed over as host of
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   after the retirement of Johnny Carson in favor of Jay Leno.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Arsenio_Hall_Show">
                    from
                    <span>
                     The Arsenio Hall Show
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   He received national exposure on NBC's
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   in the summer of 1963.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Cosby">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Bill Cosby
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Carson and McMahon departed in 1962 when Carson was hired to take over from Jack Paar on NBC's
                   <i>
                    Tonight
                   </i>
                   (renamed
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   under Carson), where they would both spend the next thirty years together.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Who_Do_You_Trust%3F">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Who Do You Trust?
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Behind-the-scenes network politics embroil television executives responsible for late-night programming after 1991's retirement announcement of Johnny Carson (played by Rich Little) from
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   on NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Late_Shift_%28film%29">
                    from
                    <span>
                     The Late Shift (film)
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   A 1996 HBO TV movie called
                   <i>
                    The Late Shift
                   </i>
                   (based on Bill Carter's New York Times bestselling book of the same title) was about the network politics that occurred after the retirement of Johnny Carson from the
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   on NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helen_Kushnick">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Helen Kushnick
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Westinghouse designed
                   <i>
                    PM East/PM West
                   </i>
                   to compete with
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   , which was then hosted by Jack Paar, but Paar and his network, NBC, attracted many more viewers.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joyce_Davidson">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Joyce Davidson
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   CBS had previously attempted late-night talk shows with
                   <i>
                    The Merv Griffin Show
                   </i>
                   (19691972) and
                   <i>
                    The Pat Sajak Show
                   </i>
                   (19891990) but were unable to compete with NBC's
                   <i>
                    The Tonight Show
                   </i>
                   and these attempts were cancelled due to poor ratings.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Show_with_Stephen_Colbert">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Late Show with Stephen Colbert
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   From 1954-57, she was host and editor-in-chief of
                   <i>
                    Home,
                   </i>
                   NBC's hour-long daytime magazine program oriented toward women, which was conceived by network president Pat Weaver to complement the network's
                   <i>
                    Today
                   </i>
                   and
                   <i>
                    Tonight
                   </i>
                   programs.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arlene_Francis">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Arlene Francis
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>

            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="11315" data-url-title="friends" id="connection-expanded-43">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  43
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-43">
                  <a href="" id="jTopicImage_44_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_44" data-searched="" data-topic-id="11315" data-topic-title="Friends" id="jTopicImage_44" src="/images/connects-default.jpg"/>
                   <span class="no-copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-43">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-43" id="connection-excerpt-43">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Friends
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is an American television sitcom, created by David Crane and Marta Kauffman, which originally aired on NBC from September 22, 1994, to May 6, 2004. It lasted ten seasons and is now in syndication. It revolves around a circle of friends living in Manhattan. The series was produced by Bright/Kauffman/Crane Productions, in association with Warner Bros. Television. The original executive producers were Kevin S. Bright, Marta Kauffman, and David Crane.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-43 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-43, .show-more-connection-article-43" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-43" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-43-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-43">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Friends
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is an American television sitcom, created by David Crane and Marta Kauffman, which originally aired on NBC from September 22, 1994, to May 6, 2004. It lasted ten seasons and is now in syndication. It revolves around a circle of friends living in Manhattan. The series was produced by Bright/Kauffman/Crane Productions, in association with Warner Bros. Television. The original executive producers were Kevin S. Bright, Marta Kauffman, and David Crane.
                     <br/>
                     Kauffman and Crane began developing
                     <i>
                      Friends
                     </i>
                     under the title
                     <i>
                      Insomnia Cafe
                     </i>
                     between November and December 1993. They presented the idea to Bright, and together they pitched a seven-page treatment of the show to NBC. After several script rewrites and changes, including a second title change to
                     <i>
                      Friends Like Us
                     </i>
                     , the series was finally named
                     <i>
                      Friends
                     </i>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     Filming took place at Warner Bros. Studios in Burbank, California. The series finale on May 6, 2004, was watched by around 52.5million American viewers, making it the fifth most watched series finale in television history and the most watched episode of the decade.
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      Friends
                     </i>
                     received positive reviews throughout its run, becoming one of the most popular sitcoms of all time. The series was nominated for 62 Primetime Emmy Awards, winning the Outstanding Comedy Series award in 2002 for its eighth season. The show ranked no. 21 on
                     <i>
                      TV Guide'
                     </i>
                     s 50 Greatest TV Shows of All Time and no. 7 on
                     <i>
                      Empire
                     </i>
                     magazine's The 50 Greatest TV Shows of All Time. In 1997, the episode "The One with the Prom Video" was ranked no. 100 on TV Guide's 100 Greatest Episodes of All-Time. In 2013,
                     <i>
                      Friends
                     </i>
                     ranked no. 24 on the Writers Guild of America's 101 Best Written TV Series of All Time and no. 28 on TV Guide's 60 Best TV Series of All Time. In 2014, the series was ranked by
                     <i>
                      Mundo Estranho
                     </i>
                     the Best TV Series of All Time.
                     <br/>
                     The show led the Nielsen ratings with its eighth season and finished among the top five every year from 1995 to 2004.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-43" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-43, #show-more-connection-article-43" href="#" id="show-less-43">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-44">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-44" id="connection-excerpt-44">
                   <b>
                    Gray Television, Inc.
                   </b>
                   is a television broadcast company headquartered in Atlanta, Georgia. Established in 1946 by James Harrison Gray, a New Englander who moved to Southwest Georgia, he formed Gray Communications System (now Gray Television) which has grown since 1993 into a modern-day, successful television group based out of Atlanta, Georgia through a series of acquisitions ranging from 1993-2014.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-44 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-44, .show-more-connection-article-44" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-44" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-44-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-44">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <b>
                      Gray Television, Inc.
                     </b>
                     is a television broadcast company headquartered in Atlanta, Georgia. Established in 1946 by James Harrison Gray, a New Englander who moved to Southwest Georgia, he formed Gray Communications System (now Gray Television) which has grown since 1993 into a modern-day, successful television group based out of Atlanta, Georgia through a series of acquisitions ranging from 1993-2014.
                     <br/>
                     Gray Television currently owns and/or operates 77 television stations in 44 television markets broadcasting 140 program streams including 76 affiliates of the Big Four networks (ABC, CBS, NBC and FOX). Gray Television's owned and/or operated stations include 26 channels affiliated with the CBS Network, 24 channels affiliated with the NBC Network, 16 channels affiliated with the ABC Network and 10 channels affiliated with the FOX Network.
                     <br/>
                     The combined Station Group owns and operates the number-one ranked television station in 28 of those 44 markets and the number-one or number-two ranked television station operations in 41 of those 44 markets. The combined TV Station Group reaches approximately 8.1 percent of total United States television households.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-44" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-44, #show-more-connection-article-44" href="#" id="show-less-44">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>

                SHOW MORE

            <li class="connection" data-id="36937" data-original-title="A television network is a telecommunications network for distribution of television program content, whereby a" data-toggle="tooltip" data-url-title="television-network" id="36937" title="">
             <a data-topic-id="36937" href="#!/36937/television-network">
              <ol class="post-list">
               <li>
                <div class="connection-counter">
