                </div>
                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="36937" data-topic-title="Television network" id="jTopicImage_46" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png/128px-DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png"/>
                 <div class="connection-title-and-excerpt">
                  <span class="connection-title" data-count="45" data-id="36937" data-url-title="television-network">
                   Television network
                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   A television network is a telecommunications network for distribution of television program content, whereby a
                  </span>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </li>
              </ol>
             </a>
            </li>
            <!-- /Collapsed connection -->
            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="36937" data-url-title="television-network" id="connection-expanded-45">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  45
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-45">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png" id="jTopicImage_46_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_46" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="36937" data-topic-title="Television network" id="jTopicImage_46" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png/128px-DuMont_Affiliates_1949.png"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-45">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-45" id="connection-excerpt-45">
                   A
                   <b>
                    television network
                   </b>
                   is a telecommunications network for distribution of television program content, whereby a central operation provides programming to many television stations or pay television providers. Until the mid-1980s, television programming in most countries of the world was dominated by a small number of broadcast networks. Many early television networks (such as the BBC, NBC or CBC) evolved from earlier radio networks.
                  </p>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-45">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-45" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-45, #show-more-connection-article-45" href="#" id="show-less-45">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
              </div>

               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Television network
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  The
                  <b>
                   National Broadcasting Company
                  </b>
                  (
                  <b>
                   NBC
                  </b>
                  ) is an American commercial broadcast television and radio network that is the flagship property of NBCUniversal, a subsidiary of Comcast.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  NBC set up the first permanent coast-to-coast radio network in the United States by 1928, using dedicated telephone line technology.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television_network" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Television network
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Many early television networks (such as the BBC, NBC or CBC) evolved from earlier radio networks.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television_network" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Television network
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>
               <a class="show-more-connection-texts more" data-to-hide="#show-more-connection-texts-45" data-to-show="#more-connection-texts-45" href="#" id="show-more-connection-texts-45">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-45">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The
                   <b>
                    Big Three television networks
                   </b>
                   are the three traditional commercial broadcast television networks in the United States: ABC, CBS and NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Three_television_networks">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Big Three television networks
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The
                   <b>
                    DuMont Television Network
                   </b>
                   (also known as the
                   <b>
                    DuMont Network
                   </b>
                   , simply
                   <b>
                    DuMont
                   </b>
                   /
                   <b>
                    Du Mont
                   </b>
                   , or (incorrectly)
                   <b>
                    Dumont
                   </b>
                   ) was one of the world's pioneer commercial television networks, rivalling NBC and CBS for the distinction of being first overall in the USA.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DuMont_Television_Network">
                    from
                    <span>
                     DuMont Television Network
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The company's stations are affiliates of various television networks: ABC, CBS, NBC and Fox.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinclair_Broadcast_Group">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Sinclair Broadcast Group
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   In American television terminology, a
                   <b>
                    fourth network
                   </b>
                   is a reference to a fourth broadcast (over-the-air) television network, as opposed to the Big Three television networks that dominated U.S. television from the 1950s to the 1990s: ABC, CBS and NBC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourth_television_network">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Fourth television network
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Unlike the five major commercial broadcast television networks in the United States, ABC, CBS, NBC, Fox and The CW  which compensate their affiliate stations to carry their programs  PBS is not a network but a program distributor that provides television content and related services to its member stations.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PBS">
                    from
                    <span>
                     PBS
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <b>
                    NBC Weather Plus
                   </b>
                   was an American weather-oriented digital broadcast and cable television network that was owned as a joint venture between NBC Universal and the local affiliates of the NBC television network.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC_Weather_Plus">
                    from
                    <span>
                     NBC Weather Plus
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The network was not a full-time television network like CBS, NBC, or ABC.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NTA_Film_Network">
                    from
                    <span>
                     NTA Film Network
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The
                   <b>
                    National Broadcasting Company (NBC)
                   </b>
                   is an American broadcast television television network owned by the NBCUniversal Television Group division of NBCUniversal, which originated as a radio network in November 1926 and expanded into television in April 1939.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_NBC_television_affiliates_%28by_U.S._state%29">
                    from
                    <span>
                     List of NBC television affiliates (by U.S. state)
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   The best-known commercial broadcasters in the United States today are the ABC, CBS, Fox and NBC television networks and the iHeartMedia radio network, based in the United States.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_broadcasting">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Commercial broadcasting
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   While UHF-TV has been available to American TV broadcasters since 1952, affiliates of the four major American TV networks (NBC, CBS, ABC, and DuMont) continued to transmit their programs primarily on VHF channels wherever they were available.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UHF_television_broadcasting">
                    from
                    <span>
                     UHF television broadcasting
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   It is most famous for housing the NBC television network headquarters.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GE_Building">
                    from
                    <span>
                     GE Building
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Four in One
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is the umbrella title for a wheel series broadcast in the United States on the NBC television network as part of its 1970-71 schedule in the Wednesday 10 PM Eastern time slot.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Four_in_One">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Four in One
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                </ul>

                <div class="box">
                 <img class="jTopicImage" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="142724" data-topic-title="Golden Globe Award" id="jTopicImage_48" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/09/Golden_Globe_Trophy.jpg/128px-Golden_Globe_Trophy.jpg"/>

                  </span>
                  <span class="connection-excerpt">
                   The Golden Globe Award is an American accolade bestowed by the 93 members of the Hollywood Foreign Press
                  </span>

                </div>
               </li>

             </a>

            <!-- /Collapsed connection -->
            <!-- Expanded Connection -->
            <li class="connection-expanded" data-id="142724" data-url-title="golden-globe-award" id="connection-expanded-47">
             <div class="connection-scroll">
              <div class="connection-article-wrapper">
               <!-- Connection Article -->
               <ol class="post-list">
                <li>
                 <div class="connection-counter">
                  47
                 </div>
                 <div class="topic-image" id="connection-image-holder-47">
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Golden_Globe_Trophy.jpg" id="jTopicImage_48_src" target="_blank">
                   <img class="jTopicImage_48" data-searched="1" data-topic-id="142724" data-topic-title="Golden Globe Award" id="jTopicImage_48" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/09/Golden_Globe_Trophy.jpg/128px-Golden_Globe_Trophy.jpg"/>
                   <span class="copyright">
                    
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-47">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-47" id="connection-excerpt-47">
                   The
                   <b>
                    Golden Globe Award
                   </b>
                   is an American accolade bestowed by the 93 members of the Hollywood Foreign Press Association (HFPA) recognizing excellence in film and television, both domestic and foreign. The annual formal ceremony and dinner at which the awards are presented is a major part of the film industry's awards season, which culminates each year with the Academy Awards.
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-47 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-47, .show-more-connection-article-47" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-47" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-47-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-47">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     The
                     <b>
                      Golden Globe Award
                     </b>
                     is an American accolade bestowed by the 93 members of the Hollywood Foreign Press Association (HFPA) recognizing excellence in film and television, both domestic and foreign. The annual formal ceremony and dinner at which the awards are presented is a major part of the film industry's awards season, which culminates each year with the Academy Awards.
                     <br/>
                     The 72nd Golden Globe Awards, honoring the best in film and television for 2014, were presented on January 11, 2015, at the Beverly Hilton Hotel in Beverly Hills, California, where they have been held annually since 1961.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-47" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-47, #show-more-connection-article-47" href="#" id="show-less-47">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>

                <li>
                 <p>
                  NBC holds the broadcast rights to several annual specials and award show telecasts including the Golden Globe Awards, the Emmy Awards (which is rotated across all four major networks each year), and two of the three pageants organized by the Miss Universe Organization: the Miss Universe and Miss USA pageants (NBC also held rights to the Miss Teen USA pageant from 2003, when NBC also assumed rights to the Miss USA and Miss Universe pageants as part of a deal brokered by Miss Universe Organization owner Donald Trump that gave the network half-ownership of the pageants, until 2007, when NBC declined to renew its contract to carry Miss Teen USA, effectively discontinuing televised broadcasts of that event).

                   from
                   <span>

                   </span>
                  </a>

                    <p>
                     <b>
                      TBS
                     </b>
                     is an American basic cable and satellite television channel that is owned by the Turner Broadcasting System division of Time Warner, which shares its name with the channel. TBS carries a variety of programming, with a focus on comedy, along with some sports events, including Major League Baseball and portions of the NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship.
                     <br/>
                     As of February 2015, TBS is available to approximately 96.5 million pay television households (82.9% of households with at least one television set) in the United States.

                Lorne Michaels
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Silverman later admitted he "never liked Al Franken to begin with," and the sketch ruined Franken's chance of succeeding Lorne Michaels as executive producer of
                  <i>
                   SNL
                  </i>
                  following his 1981 departure (with the position going to Jean Doumanian, who was fired after one season following declining ratings and negative critical reviews. Michaels would later return to the show in 1985).
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Michaels is also the executive producer of NBC show
                  <i>
                   Late Night,
                  </i>
                  and was the executive producer of
                  <i>
                   30 Rock
                  </i>
                  and
                  <i>
                   Up All Night
                  </i>
                  during their runs.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorne_Michaels" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Lorne Michaels
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>
                  Once again, NBC briefly considered cancelling the show, but programming head Brandon Tartikoff (who was something of an
                  <i>
                   SNL
                  </i>
                  fan) decided to continue the show and re-hire producer Lorne Michaels.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live_%28season_11%29" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Saturday Night Live (season 11)
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
               </ul>

                SHOW MORE
               </a>
               <div class="more-connection-texts" id="more-connection-texts-49">
                <ul class="story-list">
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   In October 1975, rival network NBC began airing the late night comedy show
                   <i>
                    NBC's Saturday Night
                   </i>
                   , which was created and produced by Lorne Michaels.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live_with_Howard_Cosell">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Saturday Night Live with Howard Cosell
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   In 1981 they co-wrote Steve Martin's fourth NBC special "Steve Martin's Best Show Ever" with such notable comedy writers as Eric Idle, Dan Aykroyd, and Lorne Michaels.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Gammill_and_Max_Pross">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Tom Gammill and Max Pross
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   In 1984, she appeared on nine episodes of
                   <i>
                    The New Show
                   </i>
                   , another NBC sketch comedy show produced by
                   <i>
                    Saturday Night Live
                   </i>
                   creator Lorne Michaels.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valri_Bromfield">
                    from
                    <span>
                     Valri Bromfield
                    </span>
                   </a>
                  </p>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <p>
                   Canadian born Lorne Michaels, who had moved from Toronto to Los Angeles in 1968 to work on Rowan and Martin's
                   <i>
                    Laugh-In
                   </i>
                   , launched the NBC comedy show
                   <i>
                    Saturday Night Live
                   </i>
                   in 1975.
                   <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canadian_humour">
                    from
                    <span>

                    </span>

                 <div class="holder connection-article" id="connection-article-50">
                  <p class="show-more-connection-article-50" id="connection-excerpt-50">
                   <i>
                    <b>
                     Meet the Press
                    </b>
                   </i>
                   is a weekly American television news/interview program that is broadcast on NBC. It is the longest-running program in American television history, though its current format bears little resemblance to the one it debuted with on November 6, 1947. Like similar shows that have followed it,
                   <i>
                    Meet the Press
                   </i>
                   specializes in interviews with
                  </p>
                  <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-50 more" data-to-hide="#connection-excerpt-50, .show-more-connection-article-50" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-50" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-50-short">
                   <span>
                    SHOW MORE
                   </span>
                  </a>
                  <div class="more-connection-article" id="more-connection-article-50">
                   <div class="holder">
                    <p>
                     <i>
                      <b>
                       Meet the Press
                      </b>
                     </i>
                     is a weekly American television news/interview program that is broadcast on NBC. It is the longest-running program in American television history, though its current format bears little resemblance to the one it debuted with on November 6, 1947. Like similar shows that have followed it,
                     <i>
                      Meet the Press
                     </i>
                     specializes in interviews with national leaders on issues of politics, economics, foreign policy and other public affairs, along with panel discussions that provide opinions and analysis.
                     <br/>
                     The longevity of
                     <i>
                      Meet the Press
                     </i>
                     can be illustrated in consideration of the fact that the program debuted during what was only the second official "network television season" for American television. One historical landmark of the program is that it was the first on which a sitting U.S. president, Gerald Ford, appeared on a live television network news program, which occurred on the November 9, 1975, broadcast.
                     <br/>
                     The program has been hosted by 12 different moderators to date, beginning with creator Martha Rountree. Chuck Todd, who also currently serves as political director, became the current moderator in September 2014.
                     <br/>
                     Currently, the hour-long program airs in most markets at 9:00 a.m. (transmitted live-to-air in the Eastern Time Zone and on tape delay elsewhere), though its timeslot may vary depending on the market due to commitments by affiliate to air religious, educational or local news, paid and public affairs programming;
                     <i>
                      Meet the Press
                     </i>
                     is also occasionally pre-empted due to sports events held outside of the U.S. that necessitate live network coverage in the morning (such as the French Open tennis tournament or the Monaco Grand Prix). The program is also rebroadcast on Sundays at 2:00 p.m. and early Monday mornings at 4:00 a.m. Eastern Time on MSNBC (whose audio feed is also simulcast on Sirius/XM Satellite Radio), and on early Monday mornings as part of NBC's "All Night" lineup. The program is also syndicated by Westwood One to various radio stations around the United States, as well as on C-SPAN Radio as part of its replays of the Sunday morning talk shows.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <a class="show-less-connection-article less" data-to-hide="#more-connection-article-50" data-to-show="#connection-excerpt-50, #show-more-connection-article-50" href="#" id="show-less-50">
                    SHOW LESS
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
               </ol>
               <a class="show-more-connection-article show-more-connection-article-50 show-more-connection-article-long more" data-to-hide=".show-more-connection-article-50" data-to-show="#more-connection-article-50" href="#" id="show-more-connection-article-50-long">
                SHOW MORE
               </a>
              </div>

               <h4>
                <span>
                 How
                </span>
                NBC
                <br/>
                <span>
                 Connects To
                </span>
                Meet the Press
               </h4>
               <ul class="story-list">
                <li>
                 <p>
                  NBC News programming includes the morning news/interview program
                  <i>
                   Today
                  </i>
                  from 7:0011:00a.m. weekdays, 7:009:00 on Saturdays and 7:008:00 on Sundays; nightly editions of
                  <i>
                   NBC Nightly News
                  </i>
                  (whose weekend editions are occasionally subject to abbreviation or preemption due to sports telecasts overrunning into the program's timeslot), the Sunday political talk show
                  <i>
                   Meet the Press
                  </i>
                  , weekday early-morning news program
                  <i>
                   Early Today
                  </i>
                  and newsmagazine
                  <i>
                   Dateline NBC
                  </i>
                  . Late nights feature the weeknight talk shows
                  <i>
                   The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon
                  </i>
                  ,
                  <i>
                   Late Night with Seth Meyers
                  </i>
                  and
                  <i>
                   Last Call with Carson Daly
                  </i>
                  , weeknight replays of the fourth hour of
                  <i>
                   Today
                  </i>
                  and CNBC program
                  <i>
                   Mad Money
                  </i>
                  , and the sketch comedy show
                  <i>
                   Saturday Night Live
                  </i>
                  , and the LXTV-produced
                  <i>
                   1st Look
                  </i>
                  and
                  <i>
                   Open House NYC
                  </i>
                  on Saturdays (replays of the previous week's
                  <i>
                   1st Look
                  </i>
                  also air on Friday late nights on most stations).
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    NBC
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
                </li>
                <li>
                 <p>

                  <i>
                   Meet the Press
                  </i>
                  ; the radio version also adopted the new name.
                  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meet_the_Press" target="_blank">
                   from
                   <span>
                    Meet the Press
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </p>
